201406	18	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Lorie Logan.	61	6
201406	19	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	61	6
201406	20	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Over the intermeeting period, market participants were focused on two ongoing themes:  the decline in longer-term interest rates, and the low levels of volatility across financial markets.	61	6
201406	21	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	I will focus on these two developments before turning to the ECB’s recent policy actions.	61	6
201406	22	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Simon will review Desk operations and discuss two memos on the effective federal funds rate and overnight RRP counterparty framework that you received in advance of the meeting today.	61	6
201406	23	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-left panel of your first exhibit, domestic financial conditions eased a bit over the period, continuing a broad trend since the December FOMC meeting.	61	6
201406	24	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Longer-term US interest rates have declined—driven almost entirely by declines in real rates—while corporate credit spreads have narrowed and equity prices have increased.	61	6
201406	25	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	This easing in conditions has occurred against a backdrop of highly accommodative monetary policy from major developed-economy central banks, including the ECB.	61	6
201406	26	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	The pronounced decline in longer-term tenors has occurred across advanced foreign economies despite important differences in their economic and policy outlooks.	61	6
201406	27	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-right panel, the US, UK, and German five-year, five-year forward nominal rates are about 65 to 90 basis points lower since December.	61	6
201406	28	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Market participants cite a variety of potential drivers for the declines, but do express some puzzlement over the extent of the moves.	61	6
201406	29	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	To better understand the drivers, the Desk’s dealer and buy-side surveys asked respondents to rate the importance of various factors in explaining the decline in the five-year, five-year forward Treasury rate since the end of last year.	61	6
201406	30	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the middle-left panel, on average, respondents assigned the highest importance to three factors: a decline in the expected level of the long-run real federal funds rate, changes in economic and policy outlooks in other advanced economies, and “market- related factors,” which includes things such as portfolio reallocation, positioning, and safe-haven flows.	61	6
201406	31	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Changes to the US economic outlook and the accumulation of US dollar reserves were viewed as somewhat less important, although as you can see, buy-side participants placed more weight than dealers on reserve accumulation as a factor.	61	6
201406	32	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	The Desk’s surveys provide further evidence of the importance of a decline in the expected level of the long-run federal funds rate as a contributor to the decline in longer-dated forwards.	61	6
201406	33	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the middle-right panel, the distribution of dealer estimates of the longer-run target rate shifted down between the December and June surveys, with the median and modal responses declining from 4 percent to 3.5 percent.	61	6
201406	34	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	The buy-side survey also shows a decline in expectations for the longer-run rate.	61	6
201406	35	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	In commentary explaining revisions to these expectations, dealers principally highlighted reductions in estimates of potential GDP growth.	61	6
201406	36	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Additionally, many have highlighted comments reportedly made by former Chairman Bernanke during recent private speaking engagements that he does not expect the federal funds rate to reach 4 percent in his lifetime.	61	6
201406	37	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Notably, roughly one-third of dealers expect some downward revisions to the SEP projections for the longer-run target rate.	61	6
201406	38	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	As I noted, survey respondents also rated changes in the economic and policy outlooks in other advanced economies as an important contributor.	61	6
201406	39	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Commentary over the period highlighted building expectations for additional accommodation from the ECB, which reportedly pressured euro-area sovereign yields lower, increasing the relative attractiveness of Treasury securities.	61	6
201406	40	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Lastly, survey respondents rated market-related factors highly.	61	6
201406	41	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Desk contacts have pointed to a reversal of positions from investors who came into 2014 betting on an increase in rates as one such factor.	61	6
201406	42	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	This view is supported by net speculative positioning in 10-year Treasury futures, which has moved closer to neutral after starting the year significantly short.	61	6
201406	43	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	In contrast to longer-term rates, the market-implied federal funds rate path is little changed since December, as shown in the bottom-left panel, and currently lies below the median of Committee participants’ target rate projections in the March SEP.	61	6
201406	44	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Most dealer and buy-side survey respondents continue to see the second half of 2015 as having the highest probability of liftoff, roughly in line with market pricing, and do not expect material changes to the 2015 or 2016 rate projections in the forthcoming SEP.	61	6
201406	45	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Among those who do expect changes to these nearer-term rate projections, views are roughly evenly split on the likely direction of those changes.	61	6
201406	46	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	In sum, while expectations for the path of policy rates over the next several years appear little changed since December, the evidence suggests that a significant portion of the decline in longer-dated forward rates is due to declines in longer-run policy rate expectations.	61	6
201406	47	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	A number of other factors also appear to have depressed term premiums.	61	6
201406	48	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	One other factor that Desk contacts have linked to the declines in longer-term interest rates is the low level of realized and implied interest rate volatility, the second theme in focus over the period.	61	6
201406	49	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	In fact, low volatility is a phenomenon that extends broadly across financial markets.	61	6
201406	50	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the bottom-right panel, implied volatilities in equity, currency, and interest rate markets are currently at or near their lows since these markets developed in the 1990s and around levels prevailing just prior to the financial crisis.	61	6
201406	51	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	While the panel shows options with one-month expiries, implied volatility on options with longer expiries has also generally declined, albeit not to historical lows.	61	6
201406	52	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	The Desk’s surveys asked respondents to rate the importance of various factors in explaining declines in implied volatility across markets.	61	6
201406	53	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-left panel of your next exhibit, respondents on average rated “investor reach-for-yield behavior” and “low levels of realized volatility” as the most important factors.	61	6
201406	54	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Reduced uncertainty about central bank reaction functions and the global economic outlook were viewed as relatively less important.	61	6
201406	55	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Reach-for-yield behavior in this context might be interpreted as investor willingness to sell options even when the expected returns to doing so are unduly low, in an effort to boost portfolio returns amid exceptionally low levels of interest rates.	61	6
201406	56	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Desk contacts report that selling options to enhance yield is being employed in larger size by a wider array of market participants.	61	6
201406	57	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	A reach for yield amid these low interest rates and volatility has likely contributed to the appreciation of various risk asset prices over recent months.	61	6
201406	58	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-right panel, high-yield corporate credit spreads to Treasury securities have narrowed significantly and are near historical lows.	61	6
201406	59	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Similarly, emerging market asset prices have risen and EM sovereign and corporate spreads have narrowed.	61	6
201406	60	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	This has occurred despite a broad downgrade of EM growth prospects and uneven improvements in addressing economic imbalances across countries.	61	6
201406	61	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Risk asset prices in the euro area have also risen over recent months, driven in large part by building expectations for ECB policy actions.	61	6
201406	62	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	The ECB signaled its willingness to ease policy at its May meeting and announced a variety of easing measures at its meeting earlier this month; taken together, these measures exceeded most market participants’ expectations.	61	6
201406	63	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Specifically, the ECB cut its main refinancing rate to 15 basis points and deposit rate to negative 10 basis points.	61	6
201406	64	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	It also lowered the marginal lending facility rate to 40 basis points.	61	6
201406	65	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	In addition, it announced targeted long-term refinancing operations linked to bank lending, extended the fixed-rate full allotment stance, suspended the sterilization of its Securities Market Program, and announced that it would intensify preparatory work related to outright purchases in ABS markets.	61	6
201406	66	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Since the May ECB meeting, broad euro-area financial conditions have eased.	61	6
201406	67	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Expectations for the path of policy rates in the euro area have pushed out considerably, with futures rates now implying EONIA will first reach 25 basis points in early 2017, out from spring 2016, and the euro has depreciated over 2 percent against the US dollar.	61	6
201406	68	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	The easing in conditions has been especially pronounced in the periphery.	61	6
201406	69	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	As seen in the middle-left panel, peripheral equity indexes have increased as much as 7 percent, while 10-year Spanish and Italian spreads to German equivalents have narrowed as many as 20 basis points.	61	6
201406	70	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	In addition, there have been reports of credit lines for peripheral banks opening up in recent days as institutions search for positive yield.	61	6
201406	71	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Despite the positive impact on asset prices and market conditions, building expectations for ECB action appear to have only modestly affected euro-area inflation expectations.	61	6
201406	72	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the middle-right panel, the recent increase in measures of shorter-dated forward inflation compensation has only partially offset the earlier declines, and they remain well below the ECB’s objective of close to, but below, 2 percent over the medium term.	61	6
201406	73	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	However, longer-dated measures of euro-area inflation compensation have remained relatively stable.	61	6
201406	74	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	The ECB actions also prompted notable declines in euro-area money market rates.	61	6
201406	75	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the bottom-left panel, forward EONIA rates have declined between 10 and 20 basis points since the May meeting.	61	6
201406	76	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	While EONIA spot and forward rates have thus far remained positive, we understand there may be some interbank overnight unsecured trades taking place at negative rates, while offered rates on overnight repo against core euro-area sovereign collateral have turned negative, as shown in the bottom-right panel.	61	6
201406	77	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	To avoid negative rates, investors are attempting to term out their euro-area money market investments when they can, though this may become increasingly challenging.	61	6
201406	78	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	German bills rates are already offered at negative rates out to 12 months and French bills are offered at negative rates out to 6 months.	61	6
201406	79	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	Despite the negative rates, the Desk has not yet heard of material dislocations in euro-area money markets.	61	6
201406	80	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	However, the impact on market functioning may become more pronounced as additional excess liquidity is introduced to the financial system with the suspension this week of SMP sterilization and the start of targeted LTROs in September.	61	6
201406	81	2014-06-18	meeting	LOGAN	I will now turn it over to Simon.	61	6
201406	82	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	To continue Lorie’s discussion of euro-area money markets, negative short-term rates pose challenges for the investment of the SOMA and ESF euro portfolios, given the goals of both ensuring adequate liquidity and preserving the principal balance of foreign currency holdings.	61	6
201406	83	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the top-left panel of your third exhibit, over the last few days we have lowered holdings of euro reverse repos, which would earn negative returns, and moved investments into official deposits, which currently earn either zero or a small positive return.	61	6
201406	84	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	We have not until today invested in market instruments at negative rates; however, given the Euro system’s decision to apply a minus 15 basis point rate on top of the negative 10 basis point deposit rate on cash accounts over 100 million euro, we have decided to temporarily invest in market instruments with mildly negative rates.	61	6
201406	85	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	As well as continuing to evaluate all options at official institutions, the Desk will increase the duration of the portfolio’s outright bond holdings.	61	6
201406	86	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Continuing with foreign operations, as explained in the memo that Steve Kamin and I sent to the Committee on June 6, the Bank of England, Bank of Japan, ECB and Swiss National Bank announced earlier today that their routine 7-day dollar auctions will continue for at least another two months beyond July 31.	61	6
201406	87	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Although they phased out their 84-day auctions, these central banks expressed the view that continuing 7-day operations would be prudent in light of potential systemic instability in dollar funding markets.	61	6
201406	88	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Their current plan is to evaluate on a monthly basis whether to announce further extensions of the scheduled auctions.	61	6
201406	89	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Recall that the recent usage of the liquidity swap lines has been minimal.	61	6
201406	90	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Turning to domestic operations, the overnight RRP exercise continues to serve as a floor for overnight rates.	61	6
201406	91	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Treasury bill supply decreased significantly in April and May, consistent with the typical seasonal pattern.	61	6
201406	92	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Historically, ongoing declines in Treasury supply have put downward pressure on GC repo rates.	61	6
201406	93	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	However, GC repo rates did not decline significantly this year, as shown in the top-right panel.	61	6
201406	94	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Rather, take-up at our operations increased sharply—shown in the middle-left panel—and the GCF repo index printed consistently above the 5 basis points offered on our operations.	61	6
201406	95	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Over the past few weeks, bill and other Treasury supply have increased, likely leading to increases in GC repo rates and large declines in overnight RRP take- up.	61	6
201406	96	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Looking ahead to quarter-end, market participants generally expect that participation in the overnight RRP exercise will increase notably.	61	6
201406	97	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	As banks and dealers cut back on the amount of overnight investments that they offer to money funds, interest in our operations is expected to increase.	61	6
201406	98	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Of note, over the past two quarter-end periods, take-up has increased by an average of about $160 billion in the week leading up to quarter-end.	61	6
201406	99	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	The staff also continues to test the TDF.	61	6
201406	100	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	As part of the current testing plan, the maximum award amount and offered rate are being gradually increased.	61	6
201406	101	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Take-up at operations, shown in the middle-right panel, has increased significantly as a result.	61	6
201406	102	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	The offered rate will increase over the next three operations, to a maximum of no more than 30 basis points.	61	6
201406	103	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Market participants estimate that take-up could reach $100 billion or more over the remainder of the testing period, which extends through early July.	61	6
201406	104	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Banks suggest that as long as the rate offered on TDF deposits remains only modestly higher than the IOER rate, participation and usage in the exercise will be limited.	61	6
201406	105	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	A significant spread is likely necessary to encourage take-up since, unlike reserves, TDF deposits do not count toward an institution’s high quality liquid assets in the LCR.	61	6
201406	106	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	However, if banks had the option to withdraw funds before the specified maturity date, TDF deposits could become LCR-compliant.	61	6
201406	107	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	As discussed in the memo you received last week, staff have developed plans for preliminary testing of a variation of the TDF that would include an early-withdrawal feature.	61	6
201406	108	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Under any such testing, a penalty rate would be charged to firms for breaking a term deposit, and it would be set at a level that would make the opportunistic early withdrawal of funds very unlikely.	61	6
201406	109	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Shifting to asset purchases, over the intermeeting period market participants pushed out their expectations for the timing of the end of SOMA reinvestments, as shown in the bottom-left panel.	61	6
201406	110	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Pooling across the dealer and buy-side surveys, the median respondent now expects MBS reinvestments to end three months after liftoff, six months later than in the April survey, though the dispersion of responses remains very wide.	61	6
201406	111	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Survey respondents and other contacts suggested that the shift to anticipating a later end to reinvestments is largely due to a speech by Vice Chairman Dudley, in which he discussed his preference to end reinvestments after the first increase in short-term interest rates.	61	6
201406	112	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	MBS market participants in particular focused on these comments and cited them as one factor contributing to the 9 basis point narrowing in option-adjusted spreads on production-coupon agency MBS over the intermeeting period.	61	6
201406	113	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	However, market participants also described the recent narrowing in OIS, shown in the bottom-right panel, as part of a longer-term trend, which they primarily attribute to limited origination.	61	6
201406	114	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	We have fully transitioned to purchasing MBS over FedTrade, the Desk’s in- house trading platform, though we continue to conduct dollar roll transactions over Tradeweb, a commercial trading platform.	61	6
201406	115	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	The switch to purchasing through large- scale auctions does not appear to have significantly changed market dynamics and staff analysis thus far indicates we are receiving better execution than the mini- auctions run on Tradeweb, consistent with standard auction theory.	61	6
201406	116	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	As was the case at the last meeting, if the FOMC chooses to decrease the pace of Treasury purchases, we will reduce the frequency of Treasury operations, while leaving the purchase distribution unchanged.	61	6
201406	117	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	If Treasury or MBS purchases are reduced, as expected by nearly all market participants, we would release a Desk statement at the same time as the Committee statement.	61	6
201406	118	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Lorie and I will have copies of the statement available for review tomorrow.	61	6
201406	119	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Finally, I will briefly review two memos you received prior to the meeting, beginning with the staff’s proposal for creating a more robust federal funds effective rate.	61	6
201406	120	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	As we have discussed in the past, and as you can see through the dotted line in the top-left panel of your final exhibit, trading volumes in the fed funds market have decreased significantly since the financial crisis.	61	6
201406	121	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	A few foreign banking organizations now comprise the majority of federal funds borrowing.	61	6
201406	122	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	The implementation of regulatory change and some of the normalization approaches the Committee is considering may further reduce activity in the market, to the point that the fed funds effective may become an inappropriate benchmark for money market conditions or an unreliable reference rate for financial contracts.	61	6
201406	123	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	The staff recommends addressing this concern in two parts.	61	6
201406	124	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	First, we intend to switch in 2015 to using FR-2420 as the source for the underlying transaction data in the calculation of the effective rate.	61	6
201406	125	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	In addition to the improved governance, the panel structure of this data may reduce complications that are caused by the changing quality-mix of firms in our brokered data set.	61	6
201406	126	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Second, we propose publishing an expanded overnight, unsecured bank funding rate that includes trading activity in Eurodollar deposits negotiated in New York.	61	6
201406	127	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Eurodollars are likely the closest alternative to fed funds.	61	6
201406	128	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Both are used by DIs to fund short-term assets, including reserve balances, and both are transacted in wholesale markets, usually at overnight tenors.	61	6
201406	129	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Moreover, as again shown in the top- left panel, Eurodollar activity brokered in New York has averaged $100 billion since 2010, more than twice the volumes in the fed funds market.	61	6
201406	130	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the top- right panel, the volume-weighted averages of the two rates tend to be very close to each other.	61	6
201406	131	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	The staff proposes two options if the Committee chooses to move forward with the introduction of an expanded rate.	61	6
201406	132	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	The first is to continue to publish the current fed funds effective rate, while also introducing a second rate, with a different name, that includes Eurodollar activity.	61	6
201406	133	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	The second is to incorporate Eurodollar activity into the current fed funds effective rate, with no change in name.	61	6
201406	134	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Under either option, the Committee could choose either to target the expanded rate or to use it as an additional indicator of money market conditions.	61	6
201406	135	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	A second staff memo you received last week reviews the counterparty framework for overnight RRP operations.	61	6
201406	136	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	As you know, the Desk conducts overnight RRPs with an expanded set of counterparties, including large money market mutual funds, GSEs, and a few depository institutions.	61	6
201406	137	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	The share of take-up in our operations by each counterparty type is shown in the middle-left panel.	61	6
201406	138	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	These counterparties were originally chosen in “waves” from 2010 to 2012 and were selected mostly for their capacity to support term draining operations.	61	6
201406	139	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Given operational constraints on our total number of counterparties and our interest in adding firms in an efficient manner, the eligibility criteria we established requires a minimum level of investable assets.	61	6
201406	140	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	We last took applications in September 2012, well before the overnight RRP exercise began.	61	6
201406	141	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	As I mentioned, the overnight RRP operations seem to provide a floor on overnight rates, which suggests that efficacy considerations do not require changes to our counterparty list.	61	6
201406	142	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	However, the Committee may consider changing the counterparty policy for other reasons.	61	6
201406	143	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	In the memo you received, the staff discussed four possible approaches, outlined in the middle-right panel.	61	6
201406	144	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	These approaches are not mutually exclusive.	61	6
201406	145	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	First, the Committee could decide to defer any decision about the counterparty list until a later date.	61	6
201406	146	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	This option may be attractive if the Committee is concerned about inadvertently signaling that overnight RRPs will become an ongoing part of the operating framework.	61	6
201406	147	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	However, we would not recommend postponing action for more than a short period of time, as a fixed counterparty list does not seem consistent with a standard Desk objective of fairness in the counterparty framework:  Fairness implies not discriminating among firms that can equally satisfy eligibility and execution objectives subject to operational constraints.	61	6
201406	148	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Many firms that are similar to current counterparties have expressed interest in participating in operations, and market participants are generally accustomed to the primary dealer framework, in which counterparties are added on a rolling basis.	61	6
201406	149	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Second, the Desk could add more counterparties of the current types, with either the current or different eligibility criteria.	61	6
201406	150	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Opening the exercise to new counterparties would address the fairness questions discussed above.	61	6
201406	151	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	If the Committee is interested in expanding the opportunity to participate in operations to a broader array of firms, one option would be to decrease the minimum assets under management for money funds.	61	6
201406	152	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Third, the Committee could choose to admit new types of firms.	61	6
201406	153	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	For example, the Desk has been approached by nonfinancial corporations, nonbank financial services companies, state and local government pension funds, and others.	61	6
201406	154	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	While this option could improve the efficacy of the overnight RRPs, it is operationally impractical and, we believe, unnecessary to extend eligibility to investors in these categories.	61	6
201406	155	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	The fourth option is to prune the existing counterparty list, so as to simplify the operating model or achieve policy objectives distinct from those usually considered by the Desk.	61	6
201406	156	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	For example, one standard reason to remove a primary dealer would be weak participation in operations, perhaps caused by a change in business model.	61	6
201406	157	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	However, in the case of the overnight RRP operations, even if a firm does not always actively participate in operations, assuming no change in business model, its counterparty status may still provide it with bargaining power that helps in the formation of a floor for overnight rates.	61	6
201406	158	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Removing counterparties for reasons unrelated to efficacy may be difficult to communicate and may also compromise the efficacy of the tool.	61	6
201406	159	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	That said, if directed by the Committee, the Desk could quickly eliminate some categories of expanded counterparties—for example, prime money market funds—and attempt to restore any loss of efficacy by adding counterparties from the remaining categories.	61	6
201406	160	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	In the interest of fairness—especially as we have not accepted applications for the program for some time—the staff recommends the second option: admitting additional firms that meet the current eligibility requirements.	61	6
201406	161	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	A few more details on the staff’s recommended approach are outlined in the bottom-left panel:  We would like to seek your consent to open a new wave in July for firms that meet the current eligibility criteria.	61	6
201406	162	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	By beginning the process soon, the staff could start the time-consuming credit, legal, and regulatory reviews.	61	6
201406	163	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	We would anticipate receiving applications from about 25 money funds, about evenly split between government and prime funds.	61	6
201406	164	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	About half of those funds would be associated with investment managers that do not currently have a fund that is a counterparty to our operations.	61	6
201406	165	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	A few additional FHLBs may also join.	61	6
201406	166	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	If the Committee chooses to use overnight RRP operations as part of its normalization strategy, the staff would recommend a switch in the future to accepting new counterparties on a rolling basis, similar to the primary dealer process.	61	6
201406	167	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	If the Committee was interested in changing the eligibility criteria—for example, by decreasing the required assets under management—that might be a convenient time to do so.	61	6
201406	168	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	61	6
201406	169	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	That concludes our prepared remarks.	61	6
201406	170	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	61	6

201406	395	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Let’s move to our discussion, then, on policy normalization, and let me just make a few remarks, if I might, to begin.	92	9
201406	396	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	First, I’d like to express my appreciation to all of you for the very engaging and productive discussion we had at our last meeting, and I very much want to thank the staff for their excellent support last time and this time as well.	92	9
201406	397	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	We covered a number of issues.	92	9
201406	398	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	We considerably clarified the area in which we’re likely to find consensus, and we succeeded, I think, in trimming down the range of options appreciably.	92	9
201406	399	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	As we resume our discussion today, let me remind everyone that we have set a goal of clearly articulating to the public our normalization strategy and framework at the time of the September meeting.	92	9
201406	400	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	This is an important deadline because I consider it essential for us to define concretely and communicate our plans well before the first steps in normalizing policy become appropriate.	92	9
201406	401	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	We will also need to provide clarity about the mechanics of our approach in order to ease the transition for market participants and to make sure that the required market infrastructure is in place.	92	9
201406	402	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Meeting this timetable will require our collective focus on some key remaining issues.	92	9
201406	403	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	In general, I think we’ve agreed that our normalization framework should allow us to deploy our mix of tools relatively flexibly to deal with contingencies that arise.	92	9
201406	404	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	But it also needs to be simple and clear enough that we can convincingly communicate it to the public.	92	9
201406	405	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Since interest rate normalization will begin at a time when our balance sheet is quite large, there’s broad consensus that raising the interest rate on excess reserves will be a central part of the rate normalization process.	92	9
201406	406	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, there are also some additional issues, and I’d like to describe, based on our previous discussion, what I’d characterize as a centrist approach.	92	9
201406	407	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	There seems to be broad, although not unanimous, agreement that the overnight RRP facility should play at least some role in our normalization plans since it would help to provide a more reliable floor for short-term rates than would IOER alone.	92	9
201406	408	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Assuming that we do operate this facility during normalization, the spread between the overnight RRP and IOER rates becomes an important issue, and at the last meeting, I heard pretty widespread support for keeping that spread rather wide.	92	9
201406	409	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	We focused on two arguments that favor maintaining a significant spread, perhaps in the neighborhood of the current 20 basis points.	92	9
201406	410	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	First, I think there is a general desire to preserve trading activity in the federal funds market; and second, given a range of uncertainties and concerns about the overnight RRP facility, there’s a desire to keep that facility modest in size.	92	9
201406	411	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	I hope we can make progress today on a number of important follow-on issues, which are spelled out in the staff memos.	92	9
201406	412	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	In particular, we need to consider the role of the federal funds, IOER, and overnight RRP rates in both the implementation and communication of monetary policy.	92	9
201406	413	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	We need to decide how to limit the financial-stability risks associated with the overnight RRP facility.	92	9
201406	414	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	We have to make choices, as Simon mentioned, relating to the modernization of the federal funds rate.	92	9
201406	415	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	And we also need to decide on our reinvestment strategy.	92	9
201406	416	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	It’s probably not essential that we reach final agreements today.	92	9
201406	417	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, if we do reach agreement on particular issues at today’s meeting, we could convey such progress to the public either through the minutes or tomorrow’s press conference.	92	9
201406	418	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	However, by the end of the July meeting, I hope we will have settled most of these substantive issues.	92	9
201406	419	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	That would allow us to finalize a set of revised normalization principles at the September meeting.	92	9
201406	420	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	We had what I thought was a very good discussion and back-and-forth on the issues last time.	92	9
201406	421	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	I hope that we can again make good use of the Q&A period after the staff presentations to make comments and ask questions that will help us all work through these complicated issues.	92	9
201406	422	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	We will also have a full go-round to make sure we hear everyone’s views on the key remaining issues, and we have purposely started very early today to allow a good deal of time for this discussion.	92	9
201406	423	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	So with those introductory remarks, let me turn the floor over to the staff.	92	9
201406	424	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	I think Gretchen is going to begin.	92	9
201406	425	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	426	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	My colleagues and I will be referring to the exhibits titled “Monetary Policy Normalization.”	92	9
201406	427	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	We will focus on three key decisions that you will need to make as you develop your approach to policy normalization.	92	9
201406	428	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	I will talk about considerations that might bear on your choice of rates to use for setting the stance of policy and communicating it to the public, then Fabio will talk about how you might choose to limit the financial-stability risks posed by an overnight RRP facility, and finally Debby will discuss the Committee’s options regarding the end of reinvestment.	92	9
201406	429	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	I’ll begin by summarizing the staff’s reading of the perspectives that you provided during the normalization go-round at the April meeting.	92	9
201406	430	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Although you expressed preliminary views and made no decisions, there appeared to be areas of common ground.	92	9
201406	431	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Staff took these areas as building blocks for a couple of approaches to policy normalization that you may find broadly acceptable, though not yet fully specified.	92	9
201406	432	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	As shown in the top panel of your first exhibit, and as the Chair just noted, in April, most of you envisioned using overnight RRPs in addition to IOER to help control short-term interest rates during the process of policy normalization.	92	9
201406	433	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	This approach could entail risks to financial stability from disruptive surges in take-up of RRPs during periods of financial stress.	92	9
201406	434	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	As a result, you expressed interest in imposing some limits on potential disruptive surges of take-up at an overnight RRP facility.	92	9
201406	435	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	In addition, you generally expressed a preference for approaches to policy normalization that would not be expected to further reduce trading in federal funds.	92	9
201406	436	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	To support such trading, you could have an appreciable spread—such as the current 20 basis point spread—between the IOER and overnight RRP rates, at least initially.	92	9
201406	437	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	An appreciable spread would also help to address your reservations about executing a very large volume of overnight RRPs with money market mutual funds and other nonbank counterparties on a regular basis.	92	9
201406	438	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	You held mixed views regarding the use of term deposits and term RRPs to drain reserves; some thought such tools could be helpful but many saw them as likely to be expensive or ineffective.	92	9
201406	439	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Even so, you generally did not wish to preclude further development and testing of term tools because it could prove useful to have them at the ready if the combination of IOER and overnight RRPs does not work as expected.	92	9
201406	440	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Two other common themes to your remarks were the desire to preserve flexibility about the longer-run policy framework, and support for developing an expanded measure of the federal funds rate.	92	9
201406	441	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Finally, you generally supported informing the public about your updated normalization plans at the time of the September FOMC meeting.	92	9
201406	442	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	If you wanted to consider approaches that incorporate these broad features, then, as noted in the middle panel, one key design issue is the role that you want the federal funds rate (or, as Simon discussed, an expanded version of that rate) to play during normalization—that is, do you want to set and communicate the stance of policy primarily by targeting the federal funds rate, or by emphasizing the administered rates on overnight RRPs and IOER?	92	9
201406	443	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Either way, you’d be using a variant of a floor system to implement policy, one with two floor rates—the IOER rate for depository institutions and the overnight RRP rate for the Federal Reserve’s RRP counterparties.	92	9
201406	444	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	We think approaches that rely on adjusting these two rates to manage short-term interest rates can be successful, whether they focus primarily on the federal funds rate or on administered rates.	92	9
201406	445	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	As noted in the bottom panel, you might want to target the federal funds rate because the rate is familiar to the public, so your communications should be well understood; making a change could risk complicating policy communications during normalization, when clear communication will be critical.	92	9
201406	446	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	You may also be inclined to use the federal funds rate now because you want to leave open using it in the longer-run policy approach after normalization is complete.	92	9
201406	447	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	If the Committee chooses to target the federal funds rate during normalization, it would also need to decide whether to use a point target, as it did prior to the financial crisis, or a target range.	92	9
201406	448	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Although current conditions in the federal funds market differ appreciably from those that prevailed when the supply of reserve balances was much smaller, you might judge that the public would most easily understand a point target for the federal funds rate, and that changes in a point target may provide a clearer signal of adjustments in the stance of monetary policy than would changes in a target range.	92	9
201406	449	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	With this approach, the FOMC would set a specific target level for the federal funds rate and direct the Desk to adjust the overnight RRP rate, perhaps within a specified range, during the intermeeting period to help keep the federal funds rate close to the point target.	92	9
201406	450	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	The Board would set the IOER rate at an appropriate spread to the federal funds target.	92	9
201406	451	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Because entities with direct access to overnight RRPs should not be willing to lend overnight in unsecured markets at a rate below the overnight RRP rate, an increase in the overnight RRP rate should put upward pressure on rates in short-term unsecured funding markets and help to move the federal funds rate back up toward its target when it falls below.	92	9
201406	452	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Similarly, reducing the overnight RRP rate should put downward pressure on the federal funds rate.	92	9
201406	453	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	However, this approach is untested.	92	9
201406	454	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	As such, the Committee might also need to authorize the use of term reserve draining tools, on a contingent basis, in case they prove necessary to hit the point funds rate target.	92	9
201406	455	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Even so, given the high level of reserves and the reliance on new tools, the Committee might need to tolerate, at least initially, greater volatility in the level of the federal funds rate around the point target than was the case before the financial crisis.	92	9
201406	456	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Thus the Committee might want to communicate that it expects the federal funds rate to be close to the point target on average over time, but not necessarily each day.	92	9
201406	457	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Alternatively, the Committee may want to use a target range for the federal funds rate, as it does today.	92	9
201406	458	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	In particular, as I just described, in current circumstances it may be difficult to hit a point target for the federal funds rate with sufficient precision.	92	9
201406	459	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Also, if the Committee targets a range, the spread between the two administered rates likely could remain constant throughout the intermeeting period rather than being subject to adjustment, as would be the case if there is a point target.	92	9
201406	460	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Having a fixed spread between the two administered rates could be seen as desirable because it might be more efficient for the transmission of monetary policy and less disruptive for money markets than the case in which the overnight RRP rate was adjusted regularly.	92	9
201406	461	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	If it took this approach, the Committee could begin to normalize rates by announcing a higher target range for the federal funds rate, and the IOER and overnight RRP rates could be raised by the same increment, preserving their current spread.	92	9
201406	462	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	However, given the level of reserves and the use of new tools, the accompanying increase in the federal funds rate could be larger or smaller than desired, and policymakers would need to decide how to react to situations in which the federal funds rate moves outside its desired target range—for example, by making an adjustment to the administered rates.	92	9
201406	463	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Rather than focusing on the federal funds rate, you might choose to set and communicate the stance of policy primarily through the overnight RRP and IOER rates, as noted in the top panel of exhibit 2.	92	9
201406	464	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	If you took this approach, you could announce a less accommodative policy stance by raising these two administered rates by the same amount, and the Committee could state that it expects the general level of short-term market rates to rise by a broadly similar amount.	92	9
201406	465	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	You could even say that you expect short-term rates including the federal funds rate to rise by a broadly similar amount, if you wanted to focus some attention on that rate without targeting it.	92	9
201406	466	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Communicating through administered rates may afford the Committee greater leeway to take no action if short-term market rates were to move temporarily outside of their expected range, since the range would not be the primary focus of communication, though also pointing to the funds rate would probably reduce that leeway.	92	9
201406	467	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Of course, if short-term market rates were persistently outside the Committee’s desired range, then some additional adjustments in the administered rates would be necessary, perhaps even during an intermeeting period.	92	9
201406	468	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Finally, as noted in the last panel, the efficacy of your chosen approach will depend in part on your decisions about how tightly to limit take-up at the overnight RRP facility.	92	9
201406	469	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	The tighter the caps on take-up at the facility—that is, the more frequently they bind—the less the facility can be expected to exert control over short- term market interest rates.	92	9
201406	470	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	In general, the degree of control that the ON RRP facility is expected to have over short-term market interest rates has implications for your decisions about your communications strategy, but also for the effectiveness with which the stance of overnight rates is transmitted to longer-run rates and real activity.	92	9
201406	471	2014-06-18	meeting	WEINBACH	Fabio will now discuss approaches to limiting disruptive surges in take-up at the ON RRP facility as well as its total size.	92	9
201406	472	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Thank you, Gretchen.	92	9
201406	473	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	In my remarks, I will review design features and other mitigants that could lessen financial-stability concerns associated with an overnight RRP facility.	92	9
201406	474	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	These mitigants are the subject of one of the memos you received over the intermeeting period.	92	9
201406	475	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	As indicated in the top left panel of exhibit 3, the memo focuses on caps on usage as a form of circuit breaker during a period of market stress.	92	9
201406	476	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	These caps are not intended to limit average take-up at the facility under normal market conditions and are expected to bind only rarely.	92	9
201406	477	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Instead, these caps are designed to prevent a disruptive surge in take-up at the facility over a short period, which could be associated with a loss of short-term funding for financial institutions and nonfinancial firms, and to provide policymakers with some time to assess conditions and to determine whether additional responses are warranted.	92	9
201406	478	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	As noted to the right, the memo identifies two main possibilities for the design of circuit breakers: individual caps—that is, caps specific to each reverse repo counterparty (or RCP)—and an aggregate cap on potential facility usage.	92	9
201406	479	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	The main benefit of individual caps is that each RCP would know in advance the maximum amount it can invest at the facility each day.	92	9
201406	480	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	An aggregate cap instead would allow greater flexibility for allocating usage across RCPs, and could be accompanied by a market-based pricing mechanism—such as a uniform-rate auction—to allocate take- up when the cap is binding.	92	9
201406	481	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Ordinarily, the rate produced by this process would be the overnight RRP rate set by the Committee, but when the cap binds, the auction rate could be lower.	92	9
201406	482	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	The Committee may consider additional features that apply to both individual and aggregate caps.	92	9
201406	483	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Caps can be rigid (so that there is a take-up limit that cannot be exceeded) or flexible (where the limit could be exceeded, perhaps at a lower rate, when demand exceeds the stated cap).	92	9
201406	484	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	In addition, caps can be static (set in advance and unvarying) or dynamic (adjusted periodically according to a predetermined algorithm).	92	9
201406	485	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Finally, dynamic caps could be set equal to previous average usage over some period plus some amount (so additive) or equal to previous average usage multiplied by some amount (so multiplicative).	92	9
201406	486	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	As indicated in the middle left panel, in assessing advantages and disadvantages of these possible design features, the Committee may find it useful to consider a number of issues.	92	9
201406	487	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	A table in the memo summarizes these various considerations.	92	9
201406	488	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	In this briefing I will focus on three of them.	92	9
201406	489	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	First, how to effectively balance the two policy goals of controlling potentially disruptive surges in take-up and setting an effective floor on short-term rates.	92	9
201406	490	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	The caps should not be too tight:  Very low caps that often bind could virtually eliminate surges into the facility but would diminish its effectiveness in controlling rates.	92	9
201406	491	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	By contrast, very high and loose caps would have the opposite outcome, improving control over rates, but allowing potentially disruptive surges into the facility.	92	9
201406	492	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Evidence from the overnight RRP exercise to date indicates that individual take-up varies proportionally much more than aggregate take-up, so it may be difficult to set individual caps that provide enough flexibility without leaving considerable room for a surge in aggregate usage.	92	9
201406	493	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	This observation suggests that an aggregate cap may be more effective than individual counterparty caps in balancing the two policy goals, especially if accompanied by a pricing mechanism to facilitate a market-based allocation of overnight RRP when the cap binds.	92	9
201406	494	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Second, ease of implementation and burden on RCPs.	92	9
201406	495	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Current Desk systems could handle in a robust and automated fashion an aggregate cap with a uniform-price auction to allocate awards when the cap binds as well as a uniform system of individual caps.	92	9
201406	496	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	However, implementation of some other more complex possibilities—for example, a system in which the rate on the overnight RRP declines with aggregate take-up according to a specified schedule—would require a potentially significant amount of time to make changes to Desk systems.	92	9
201406	497	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	With respect to burden on RCPs, an aggregate cap paired with an auction would require RCP bids to include both a quantity and a rate that may vary.	92	9
201406	498	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	As a result, this option may be perceived as somewhat more burdensome than current operations, which only require RCPs to submit a quantity and confirm the specified ON RRP rate.	92	9
201406	499	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	However, when the aggregate cap is not expected to bind, the problem faced by RCPs would be no more complex than it is now.	92	9
201406	500	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Finally, communication issues.	92	9
201406	501	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Overall, simpler options would undoubtedly be easier to communicate.	92	9
201406	502	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Static, uniform counterparty caps, as currently used, would probably present the fewest communication challenges, but a rigid aggregate cap would also be straightforward to describe.	92	9
201406	503	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	The use of dynamic caps might present some communications challenges, at least initially.	92	9
201406	504	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Advance communication of rules for setting the level of caps, so that market participants would be familiar with the mechanics of the facility and would not necessarily interpret binding caps as signals about the Committee’s intentions, would also be advantageous.	92	9
201406	505	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	In light of the considerations outlined above, the Committee might want to focus today’s discussion on two options, highlighted in the panel to the right.	92	9
201406	506	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	The first option—an individual cap option—envisions the use of individual rigid caps that are adjusted periodically based on past usage.	92	9
201406	507	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	For example, an RCP’s cap could be set each month to its average take-up over the previous month plus an amount in a range between $1 billion and $5 billion.	92	9
201406	508	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	The rate paid is the overnight RRP set by the Committee.	92	9
201406	509	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	The second option—an aggregate cap option—involves an aggregate rigid cap that is adjusted periodically based on past usage.	92	9
201406	510	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	For example, the aggregate cap could be set each week to the average take-up over the previous week plus an amount in a range between $50 billion and $300 billion.	92	9
201406	511	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Each day, the Desk would conduct a uniform-price auction for the cap amount with a maximum allowable bid equal to the overnight RRP rate set by the Committee; because demand would rarely exceed the cap amount, RCPs would almost always be able to invest the amounts that they have requested and receive the announced overnight RRP rate.	92	9
201406	512	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	As indicated in the bottom panel, the wide range for the additive factors in these proposals reflects the difficulty of evaluating the tradeoffs between having caps set high enough to make an overnight RRP facility effective in firming rates but also low enough to limit potentially disruptive surges.	92	9
201406	513	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Both components of the tradeoff are uncertain, and more staff work during the testing phase would be needed to help inform the Committee’s choice of the additive factor.	92	9
201406	514	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	The Committee may want to consider whether setting caps so that they may bind occasionally—for example, at quarter-ends—could have salutary effects.	92	9
201406	515	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Occasionally binding caps may reduce pressures for changes in rules when caps do bind because market participants would become familiar with procedures, expect them to be followed, and temper their reliance on overnight RRP in their own contingency planning.	92	9
201406	516	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	On the other hand, caps that bind, even rarely, in normal times could also have costs—for example, by constraining the facility’s ability to accommodate quarter-end pressures.	92	9
201406	517	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	In addition to the risks associated with a sudden surge in take-up, the Committee may be concerned that dynamic caps that adjust automatically could result in a very large facility size during protracted periods of stress as the effective limit ratchets upwards, an outcome that could lead to further disruptions in funding markets.	92	9
201406	518	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Although the Federal Reserve has a number of tools at its disposal to ameliorate financial strains by injecting liquidity back into the system, several factors could limit the efficacy of these tools or temper the willingness of policymakers to use them.	92	9
201406	519	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Hence, the Committee may want to impose an ultimate limit on facility usage as a complement to dynamic caps.	92	9
201406	520	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	For example, it may set an overall facility limit of $750 billion or $1 trillion or an individual limit of $10 billion or $15 billion if individual caps are used.	92	9
201406	521	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Further staff work would be needed to calibrate this ultimate limit to balance the financial-stability risks with reduced control over rates during the normalization process.	92	9
201406	522	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	In the event that caps bind because of a surge into overnight RRP—that is, if circuit breakers are “tripped”	92	9
201406	523	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	—the Committee may face pressures from multiple constituencies.	92	9
201406	524	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	RCPs may advocate raising or eliminating the caps, while institutions facing strains in funding markets may advocate for injections of liquidity.	92	9
201406	525	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	The Committee may want to consider whether additional actions to mitigate strains would be warranted in such situations.	92	9
201406	526	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	For example, the Committee could lower the overnight RRP rate, adjust the cap, or provide liquidity.	92	9
201406	527	2014-06-18	meeting	NATALUCCI	Debby will now talk about reinvestment options.	92	9
201406	528	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	Thank you, Fabio.	92	9
201406	529	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	Turning to exhibit 4, I will cover options for when to cease or reduce reinvestments, which is another element of your normalization strategy.	92	9
201406	530	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	As noted in your top left panel, the exit principles included in the minutes of the June 2011 FOMC meeting indicated that ceasing or reducing reinvestments would likely be the first step in the process of normalization, and would be followed by modifications to forward guidance, reserve draining operations, and only then an increase in the target federal funds rate; agency securities would likely be sold sometime after that.	92	9
201406	531	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	Several important changes—noted in the top-right panel—have occurred in the three years since.	92	9
201406	532	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	They include a substantial increase in securities holdings and excess reserves; the sale of shorter-dated Treasury securities holdings during the Maturity Extension Program; changes in the forward guidance; the Committee’s indication that it no longer expects to sell agency MBS during normalization; and the development of overnight RRPs to help control interest rates with a large balance sheet.	92	9
201406	533	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	As summarized in the next panel, if the economy evolves in line with the staff’s baseline expectations, halting reinvestments six months before liftoff, at liftoff, or sometime after liftoff has relatively limited effects on estimates of the term premium and balance sheet.	92	9
201406	534	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	Accordingly, in that case, the choice does not materially affect the timing of liftoff or macroeconomic outcomes, nor does it have a discernible effect on projected remittances to the Treasury.	92	9
201406	535	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	That said, to the extent that the flow of purchases might have an effect on interest rates—a possibility that is not factored into staff models but which some market participants appear to put weight on in the MBS market—announcing a halt in reinvestments may put some upward pressure on MBS rates, which could pass through to primary mortgage rates.	92	9
201406	536	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	As noted in the middle-right panel, there are several possible options for timing an end to reinvestments as part of a revised normalization strategy—before liftoff, after liftoff, or coincident with liftoff.	92	9
201406	537	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	All else equal, ceasing reinvestments prior to liftoff—the first option—would normalize the size of the balance sheet sooner than in the other options and would slightly reduce the level of reserves prior to liftoff.	92	9
201406	538	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	In the staff’s current baseline, reserves are drained to a lesser degree (both in dollar terms and as a share of the balance sheet) than the staff originally projected in mid-2011.	92	9
201406	539	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	Because even passive reductions in security holdings are a means for removing policy accommodation, the Committee would presumably stop reinvesting principal payments only when it judged that conditions were appropriate to begin to tighten policy.	92	9
201406	540	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	However, if you are concerned that reductions in securities holdings might have an unpredictable effect on interest rates that could potentially delay liftoff, you may prefer to maintain reinvestments until sometime after liftoff—which is a second option.	92	9
201406	541	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	You also might prefer initiating policy normalization with an increase in your target for short-term interest rates in part because you have indicated that you plan to use short-term interest rates as your primary tool for adjusting the stance of monetary policy.	92	9
201406	542	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	Moreover, you might want to gain confidence in the sustainability of the tightening cycle, halting reinvestments only once you were confident that the decision was unlikely to be reversed.	92	9
201406	543	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	Some policymakers may judge it appropriate to maintain reinvestments beyond liftoff in order to limit the risk of a too-large tightening of financial conditions upon liftoff, and potentially to enhance flexibility to provide more accommodation if the economy weakens during the tightening cycle.	92	9
201406	544	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	But other policymakers may be concerned that an end to reinvestments could be delayed for a substantial period, implying that the balance sheet would not begin to shrink until much later than they judge appropriate.	92	9
201406	545	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	If you decide to end reinvestments after liftoff, you might want to adopt a trigger or threshold relative to your interest rate target, economic conditions, or time.	92	9
201406	546	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	Depending on the details of the approach taken, communications associated with an after-liftoff option could be more complicated than in the other options for stopping reinvestment.	92	9
201406	547	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	A third option would be to halt reinvestments at the same time as liftoff.	92	9
201406	548	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	Taking actions on interest rates and the balance sheet simultaneously offers simplicity in communications, but also could make the initial tightening move less gradual than starting with either tool first.	92	9
201406	549	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	Of course, ceasing reinvestments entirely is not the only alternative to reinvesting all payments of principal.	92	9
201406	550	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	As seen in the bottom panel, the monthly runoff of securities from the SOMA portfolio is quite variable in the case of Treasury securities, which start to mature in size in 2016.	92	9
201406	551	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	It is also subject to prepayment uncertainty in the case of agency MBS (for which modeled estimates are shown in the chart).	92	9
201406	552	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	If you wished to see a steady decline in the size of the portfolio, you could smooth the path by conducting partial reinvestments in months when runoff was particularly large, perhaps augmenting this strategy with sales of short-dated securities in months when runoff was small.	92	9
201406	553	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	Separately, you could use reinvestment policies to shift the allocation of assets within the portfolio—for example, by diverting MBS reinvestments into Treasury securities to expedite a return to an all- Treasury portfolio, or vice versa to provide ongoing support to the housing market.	92	9
201406	554	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	The final page of your handout provides a copy of the questions that were distributed with the staff memos on normalization.	92	9
201406	555	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	You may want to address these questions in your contributions during the go-round.	92	9
201406	556	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	Thank you, Madam Chair, that completes our prepared remarks.	92	9
201406	557	2014-06-18	meeting	LEONARD	We’d be happy to take questions.	92	9

201406	785	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	It is not obvious that now—when we’re not implementing a point target for the funds rate—provides good evidence about how the relationship between the RP rate and the funds rate would work if we were targeting the funds rate.	92	9

201406	791	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	About whether we need to decide our long-run framework or not, we’re building some machinery and we’re raising some expectations.	92	9

201406	794	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	We are raising expectations, and we are raising adjustment costs.	92	9
201406	795	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	We are inducing people to undertake investments that would be costly to reverse, and the prospect of those costs has the ability to kind of stay our hand, and make us reluctant to back away from offering RRPs on the scale and scope that we are offering them now.	92	9
