201406	1134	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Before beginning, though, I did want to commend the Chair and the staff for organizing our decision on normalization policies in the way that they have, with a series of discussions in consecutive FOMC meetings preceded by that set of introductory memos we got in April, which have now been supplemented with this additional set of memos that elaborate on some of the issues and questions raised in the April meeting.	92	9
201406	1135	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Having read last week the portion of the April transcript on normalization, I also want to note the openness with which participants considered the issues in that first discussion, the way in which the Chair encouraged productive interaction among participants, and the thoroughness with which the staff has responded in the second set of memos.	92	9
201406	1136	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	And I say all this not simply to heap praise on people, but because I actually think it has presented a template for deciding on key issues that will serve us well over the course of the next couple of years.	92	9
201406	1137	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Turning now to the substance of the set of policy issues on normalization, I don’t want to bury my lead, so I’ll say upfront that my basic reaction is a growing uneasiness at the prospect of our normalization process resulting in a large, regularized ON RRP program.	92	9
201406	1138	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	I hasten to add that I think we need to have ON RRP among the tools we use during normalization, and with respect to longer-term policies, there’s certainly merit in thinking about the idea of having ON RRP as a permanent tool of monetary policy.	92	9
201406	1139	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	So my uneasiness is grounded not in opposition to the instrument as such, but in a concern that by committing or perhaps overcommitting ourselves now to a large, sustained ON RRP facility, we could be courting unintended and possibly undesirable consequences.	92	9
201406	1140	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	At the April meeting, a number of participants commented on the potentially profound consequences for money markets and for the organization of the financial sector more generally of the creation of a large ON RRP operation.	92	9
201406	1141	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Many of us also noted the possibility that in times of stress, such an operation could exacerbate disintermediation by facilitating a run on assets carrying any credit or liquidity risk in favor of completely safe repos with the Federal Reserve.	92	9
201406	1142	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	A specific concern bridging both these observations was the possibility of the truly ironic outcome whereby the FOMC, nearly all of whose members have publicly identified money market funds as a major threat to financial stability, would have paved the track by which these funds could run from commercial paper, CDs, and other private-sector assets.	92	9
201406	1143	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	But I think the issue goes beyond this discrete though important consideration.	92	9
201406	1144	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	One might ask, for example, whether a large and permanent ON RRP facility would encourage a range of cash lenders to assume greater risk in the belief that they can quickly shift their asset composition to ON RRPs as circumstances change.	92	9
201406	1145	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Even financial actors that are not certified ON RRP counterparties might take advantage of this safest of havens through a restructuring of the interconnections of financial actors, whereby such actors would have what we might call a standing line of liability with qualified counterparties.	92	9
201406	1146	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	The staff memos for this meeting didn’t really address the potential for far-reaching change in business models of various parts of the financial sector.	92	9
201406	1147	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Indeed, it would have been asking a lot to expect such analysis in just a few weeks, based on the limited testing that has taken place to date.	92	9
201406	1148	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	The memo on counterparties seemed to assume that a greater number of counterparties was desirable precisely because of the intention to use ON RRP as a primary tool of normalization.	92	9
201406	1149	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	In any case, I don’t think we yet have a very good basis for understanding the effects a large, sustained ON RRP program would have.	92	9
201406	1150	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Among other things, I wonder whether such a program would actually be reversible after monetary policy normalization or whether some years from now its contemplated termination would be seen as too disruptive to a reshaped financial sector.	92	9
201406	1151	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	The financial-stability concerns from the previous meeting were addressed mainly through a proposal for some variant on a system of caps in order to limit the potential for a surge of disintermediation during a crisis.	92	9
201406	1152	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	The memo on financial-stability concerns considers both individual and aggregate caps but forthrightly acknowledges that it’s very difficult to determine what level of cap would best balance the presumed reliance on ON RRP to firm rates and the desire to avoid disruptive surges.	92	9
201406	1153	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Actually, though, I read the suggestion that the cap might be set at average recent use plus as much as $300 billion—the estimated amount of flight to quality in the worst week of the crisis—as tantamount to forgoing this balancing effect by having formal caps that are not practically binding.	92	9
201406	1154	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	I at least would be uncomfortable launching a normalization program that essentially subordinated financial-stability concerns to the interests of maximum control over short-term rates.	92	9
201406	1155	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	But even if we were to set caps that would be expected to bind, I think there are two concerns.	92	9
201406	1156	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	The first and lesser is that they could be a quite visible metric of the flight to quality during a period of stress, assuming that there would be something close to real-time transparency around the usage of ON RRP.	92	9
201406	1157	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	That is, they would provide a kind of play-by-play of increasing stress as funds flowed into the ON RRP program.	92	9
201406	1158	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	The second and more important concern is that the system of binding caps could lack credibility.	92	9
201406	1159	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	I think there’s some reason for skepticism that the caps would hold in a period of near-crisis, and in fact, I think the characterization by some in the morning session of these as circuit breakers or triggers rather than real caps more accurately captures the institutional dynamic that would ensue.	92	9
201406	1160	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Based on what we know and have discussed to this point, the cap system strikes me as an almost textbook case of a time-consistency problem.	92	9
201406	1161	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	We will grow the ON RRP facility and solemnly indicate that its usage has limits, but then as stress builds and the money markets in which ON RRP will have become such a major part come under pressure for capital conservation, we could be tempted to offer this safe haven without any limit but the size of our balance sheet, at least to those previously qualified as counterparties and maybe to others as well.	92	9
201406	1162	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	And, it’s important to note, that might well be the right ex post response under such circumstances, but it’s precisely for this reason that the caps may lack ex ante credibility.	92	9
201406	1163	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	A large-scale flight to quality at the Fed would mean the withdrawal of funding from lots of private balance sheets, a circumstance in which we would doubtless feel considerable pressure, policy and political, to lend the funds that we were borrowing.	92	9
201406	1164	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	In that case, we would once again be in the business of creating our alphabet facilities that de facto affect significantly where relatively scarce credit is flowing in the economy.	92	9
201406	1165	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	But in this new world, we might have morphed from being a lender of last resort to an intermediator of something less than last resort.	92	9
201406	1166	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	I think it’s hard to know how much more disintermediation would take place in a world in which the Fed was providing a safe asset whose price was, at least for a time, insensitive to increased demand over and above the amount we saw actually occur during the last financial crisis.	92	9
201406	1167	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	But it’s at least possible that it would be significantly greater and, indeed, that the existence of a large, standing ON RRP program would, by facilitating disintermediation, amplify it during moderate stress periods, such as that we experienced in the late summer of 2011.	92	9
201406	1168	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	More generally, it is possible that such a program would encourage business models of short-term intermediation that would be premised on the ability to exit quickly to a completely safe haven.	92	9
201406	1169	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	To repeat what I said at the outset, I believe we need to include ON RRP in the normalization toolkit, but, subject to further discussion today and between now and our July meeting, my current view is that we should aim for the ON RRP program to play more of a backup role.	92	9
201406	1170	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	If the program does not become and remain predictably large, the odds of unintended and perhaps not fully understood consequences are lower.	92	9
201406	1171	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Moreover, even a less prominent use of the program in pursuit of specific monetary policy ends, as opposed to simply for testing, might provide some insight into what the effects of a large, permanent program would be.	92	9
201406	1172	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	And I want to add here that I listened with interest to some of the discussion before lunch as to whether we might say at the outset that we would not continue the program after normalization was completed.	92	9
201406	1173	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	I actually think that might be a mistake as well.	92	9
201406	1174	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	I don’t know why we’d necessarily want to rule out the possibility of continuing its use as some form of a monetary policy instrument.	92	9
201406	1175	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	It’s just the growth of it and the consequences that would ensue from the early growth that concern me.	92	9
201406	1176	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Obviously, this set of concerns has implications for our choices on normalization policies, and in an effort to be at least somewhat constructive here, I’ve tried to specify for myself what I think those implications are.	92	9
201406	1177	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	First, we should rely principally on the IOER rate to affect interest rates.	92	9
201406	1178	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Second, in order to avoid the need for continuous fine-tuning using ON RRP, to the degree that we set the federal funds rate as a target—whether the current or revised version of the federal funds rate—that target should be a range rather than a specific point.	92	9
201406	1179	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	I’m not really sure whether it’s better to have this rate as a target or whether the Committee can instead simply be monitoring the effect of IOER and other instruments on relevant interest rates without setting even a target range, and on that point I’m interested to hear the views of others today.	92	9
201406	1180	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Third, so as to limit the growth of the ON RRP program, the spread should be at least the current 20 basis points.	92	9
201406	1181	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Fourth, a desire to limit, if possible, the size of the ON RRP program means we may need to use some policy tools that, considered individually, may not have seemed particularly attractive.	92	9
201406	1182	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	As is usually the case, policy decisions entail a choice among imperfect alternatives.	92	9
201406	1183	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Since each mix of policy tools carries certain risks alongside its expected efficacy, a tool should not be disqualified simply because it’s arguably less effective than another, since it may entail fewer risks.	92	9
201406	1184	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	So, for example, my uneasiness about a large ON RRP operation has caused me to rethink what was my tentative conclusion that we shouldn’t use a term deposit facility.	92	9
201406	1185	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Fifth, it’s important to note that if the approach suggested in the preceding four points did not produce the firming we desire during the normalization process, we would still be able to expand the use of ON RRPs either by increasing the universe of eligible counterparties or narrowing the spread relative to the IOER rate.	92	9
201406	1186	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	I acknowledge that this more eclectic approach compounds what is already a communications challenge for our normalization policies.	92	9
201406	1187	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	An inability to communicate our intentions and expectations with relative clarity might undermine the efficacy of the normalization process itself.	92	9
201406	1188	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	I hope that, at least as far as communication in September of our revised exit strategy is concerned, we might be able to describe something that was driven by IOER with reference to the effect on the federal funds rate or some other relevant rates, and that we could refer to other tools, including ON RRP, that would be available to firm interest rate floors if and as needed.	92	9
201406	1189	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	But here again, my own calculus of the costs and benefits of this approach would be affected by the views of others, particularly the Chair, on whom the burden of communicating on behalf of the whole Committee will fall, as to the relative communication challenges of this and different approaches.	92	9
201406	1190	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1191	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	May I ask a clarifying question?	92	9
201406	1192	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Governor Tarullo, you used the word “large” a lot in your comments.	92	9
201406	1193	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Can you give me a sense of what “large” is?	92	9
201406	1194	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Well, part of the problem  is that I haven’t been able to get a very good sense of what people are contemplating for the size of the ON RRP program as an ongoing tool to play the kind of role in a corridor system that people had contemplated.	92	9
201406	1195	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	But I have to say that it seems to me that if it got very much larger than it already is, we would begin to run some of the risks that I identified.	92	9
201406	1196	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	So $200 billion is okay?	92	9
201406	1197	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I’m just trying to get a sense of where you start to get concerned.	92	9
201406	1198	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	It’s fairly easy to say that at current levels I don’t have a high level of concern.	92	9
201406	1199	2014-06-18	meeting	TARULLO	Because of my skepticism about how well caps will hold once one is on some sort of trajectory upward, I think my concern may be as much in the way we project it and grow it initially as opposed to the size it actually ends up being.	92	9
201406	1200	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Okay.	92	9
201406	1201	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you.	92	9
201406	1202	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	President Bullard.	92	9
201406	1203	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1204	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	Let me begin by thanking the staff for the background memos on normalization issues.	92	9
201406	1205	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	I thought these were thoroughly done, touching on a wide range of topics that could influence the Committee’s future decisionmaking in this area.	92	9
201406	1206	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	I intend to simply walk through the four questions posed in the appendix of the staff memo “Overview of Additional Staff Memos on Normalization” by English and colleagues.	92	9
201406	1207	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	The first question concerns the wisdom of keeping the federal funds rate as a primary vehicle for Committee communications regarding the stance of monetary policy.	92	9
201406	1208	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	My main comment here is that I think it is risky to keep referring to the federal funds rate or its more elaborate cousin that includes Eurodollar transactions as the main policy focus of the FOMC.	92	9
201406	1209	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	With such high levels of reserves in the banking system, the federal funds rate is a mere shadow of its former self, and it seems unlikely to return to true form over the medium term.	92	9
201406	1210	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	Moreover, the expanded version—the overnight bank funding rate—may behave inappropriately in times of stress, as noted in the staff memo on the subject, possibly because of events outside US borders.	92	9
201406	1211	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	This could make for a difficult situation to manage if FOMC communications were to be squarely centered on such a rate.	92	9
201406	1212	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	The IOER rate, in my view, also has limitations because it is only applicable to the banking system, a shrinking fraction of the financial intermediation sector in the United States.	92	9
201406	1213	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	This leaves the overnight reverse repo rate, with its broader system of counterparties, as the most promising candidate for the label of policy rate.	92	9
201406	1214	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	The scenarios outlined in the staff analysis suggesting how the overnight RRP rate might be set in conjunction with the IOER rate seemed reasonable to me.	92	9
201406	1215	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	I would be open to making some reference to the federal funds rate, but obliquely and in a way that makes it clear that this particular short-term rate does not today carry the importance that it once did.	92	9
201406	1216	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	The second question posed concerns the potential circuit breakers to prevent what might be thought of as excessive take-up in the overnight reverse repo program during periods of financial stress.	92	9
201406	1217	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	After reviewing the memo on this topic, I would be willing to support, at least initially, an aggregate cap that would adjust dynamically according to relatively slowly changing macroeconomic conditions.	92	9
201406	1218	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	My sense on this is that, should a period of severe financial stress arise in which financial firms are turning to the overnight reverse repo program aggressively, we are probably going to want to allow the cap to be breached to respond to the crisis—and in this respect, I agree with the comments just made by Governor Tarullo that these are not credible caps.	92	9
201406	1219	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	But a cap would allow that decision to be made at the time.	92	9
201406	1220	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	The decision to move the cap could be made then, at the time, by the Committee and would send a signal that the Committee does not expect extraordinary usage in ordinary times.	92	9
201406	1221	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	One of the most serious issues with the overnight reverse repo program—and here again, I’m agreeing with Governor Tarullo’s comments that he just made—may be the signal being sent by the Fed to nonbank counterparties that they will now be treated almost like banks but without the regulatory apparatus that banks otherwise have.	92	9
201406	1222	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	Strictly speaking, we are saying no such thing.	92	9
201406	1223	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	But if the impression is created, market pricing can be affected nevertheless.	92	9
201406	1224	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	This aspect of the facility bears careful watching as we go forward.	92	9
201406	1225	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	So I would describe this as a medium- term to long-term industrial organization issue, as opposed to the operational issues that we have been discussing so far.	92	9
201406	1226	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	The third question involves reinvestment of principal on securities holdings.	92	9
201406	1227	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	The Committee laid out ending reinvestment as a preliminary step before raising the policy rate in the exit principles of the spring of 2011.	92	9
201406	1228	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	I’d prefer that we retain this step in the exit principles.	92	9
201406	1229	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	In my view, it is a relatively mild way to begin the removal of policy accommodation.	92	9
201406	1230	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	Certainly, the staff simulations seem to bear this out, to the extent we have reasonable models of these effects.	92	9
201406	1231	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	The Committee has wanted to get back to a more normal-size balance sheet, and the end of reinvestments would provide a relatively mild way to begin to accomplish that task.	92	9
201406	1232	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	Even those on the Committee who may be comfortable with a relatively large balance sheet probably do not desire the $4 trillion–plus size that we have now.	92	9
201406	1233	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	Among other risks, we will eventually have to pay very large sums to the largest banks in the United States, as well as large foreign banks, through IOER.	92	9
201406	1234	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	I remain concerned that this is potentially a political loser for the Fed when this time arrives.	92	9
201406	1235	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	For these reasons, I think we need to get on with ending reinvestment and reducing the size of the balance sheet when we have the opportunity.	92	9
201406	1236	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	Without the step of ending reinvestments first, in my view, there will be even more pressure on the date of policy rate liftoff, possibly pulling that date forward from when it would otherwise occur.	92	9
201406	1237	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	Also, I would be open to more graduated or managed approaches to ending reinvestment should the Committee wish to go in that direction.	92	9
201406	1238	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	We talked a little bit about that in the question-and-answer session earlier.	92	9
201406	1239	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	So I think it could be done—instead of just saying, “End reinvestment,” you could do it in a way that said, “We want the balance sheet to go down at a certain pace.”	92	9
201406	1240	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	And I think that would be fine.	92	9
201406	1241	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	The fourth question concerns the idea of an expanded definition of the federal funds rate.	92	9
201406	1242	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	In answer to the first question just now, I noted that a definitionally revamped overnight bank funding rate may not behave well in a time of financial stress, possibly because of developments outside the United States, according to a staff memo.	92	9
201406	1243	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	This seems to suggest to me that we would not want to go in this direction.	92	9
201406	1244	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	The definitionally-revamped overnight bank funding rate would behave well when it does not matter—that is, when fed funds and Eurodollar transactions occur at the same price—and may behave poorly when it does matter—that is, in times of stress.	92	9
201406	1245	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	If this is the case, why do it?	92	9
201406	1246	2014-06-18	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1247	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201406	1248	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	President Rosengren.	92	9
201406	1249	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1250	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	This is our third crack at crafting an exit strategy.	92	9
201406	1251	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	The second proposed exit strategy looked quite different than the first.	92	9
201406	1252	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	This announcement is likely to be quite different than the first or the second.	92	9
201406	1253	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	That we have changed our strategy as the size of our balance sheet and economic circumstances have changed is quite reasonable.	92	9
201406	1254	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, our communication of strategies that were highly dependent on future circumstances was not as effective as we might have liked.	92	9
201406	1255	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	That should provide a significant caution as we consider our future strategy and accompanying communications.	92	9
201406	1256	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	There are many questions we cannot know the answer to until we have begun the process of normalization.	92	9
201406	1257	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	For example, we do not know how strong the gravitational pull of interest on excess reserves will be on market interest rates as we raise the IOER rate or as we face periods of financial turbulence.	92	9
201406	1258	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	We do not know the size of the take-up of our reverse repo facility, both as we raise rates and as institutions like government money market funds adjust to the new facility.	92	9
201406	1259	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Nor do we know the extent to which counterparties will flock to our facility during periods of financial turbulence, or how much the use of our reverse repo facility might reduce the willingness to lend to the private sector during periods of financial turbulence.	92	9
201406	1260	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	This facility works primarily through money market funds.	92	9
201406	1261	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	The SEC is considering significant regulatory changes to money market funds.	92	9
201406	1262	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	The money market fund industry may go through significant change as a result of this facility and the SEC regulatory changes.	92	9
201406	1263	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	And the nature of these structural changes and their effects on short-term markets are hard to predict at this time.	92	9
201406	1264	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	These are but a few questions that, I think, will be important to better understand over time.	92	9
201406	1265	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	There are many others.	92	9
201406	1266	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, uncertainty does not excuse inaction, but it is a reason to admit to ourselves and the public that this will be somewhat experimental.	92	9
201406	1267	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	No central bank has exited with this balance sheet and set of instruments before.	92	9
201406	1268	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	How we proceed and what our final destination will be are likely to be influenced by what we learn along the way.	92	9
201406	1269	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	If we provide too rigid a set of principles in our initial communications, we risk misleading rather than informing the public.	92	9
201406	1270	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	We can, of course, only make decisions based on what we know now.	92	9
201406	1271	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	But what I am counseling is building flexibility into our processes and communications, consistent with the limits of our current knowledge and with our willingness to adjust as we learn more.	92	9
201406	1272	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Our earlier set of exit announcements were necessarily constrained by our knowledge at that time, but they were received by the market as a set of relatively rigid guidelines for exit, which they probably should not and could not have been.	92	9
201406	1273	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Turning to the questions posed to us in the memos, first, our communication strategy should be clear and simple.	92	9
201406	1274	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	We should announce that we are setting the interest rate on excess reserves as our policy tool.	92	9
201406	1275	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	While we should announce that we plan to initially maintain the reverse repo rate at roughly a 15 to 20 basis point discount to the rate of interest on excess reserves, we should make clear that we may alter the spread over time depending on economic circumstances and our experience using these instruments to affect short-term market interest rates.	92	9
201406	1276	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would be opposed to announcing we are targeting the federal funds rate, or any other market rate, until we obtain a better understanding of how the facility functions.	92	9
201406	1277	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	We should gather more information from the first several tightening actions and then decide, with much fuller information than we have now, about the costs and benefits of moving from administered rates to another set of rates in our communication.	92	9
201406	1278	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Turning to question 2, the main counterparties to this facility are government and prime money market funds.	92	9
201406	1279	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	There has not been much discussion of the implications of this new facility working largely through private money market funds, particularly at a time when the SEC’s regulation is in flux.	92	9
201406	1280	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	In addition, money market funds are likely to make more adjustments once the parameters of our program are announced.	92	9
201406	1281	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	As for the cap alternatives, since money funds, particularly some wholesale funds, can have quite variable flows, individual caps may be complex and burdensome and during times of stress may even be perverse.	92	9
201406	1282	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	For example, if wholesale investors become worried about a large fund, and there is a significant shift to another fund family, would we want credit concerns about specific fund families to lead to binding individual caps?	92	9
201406	1283	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	This could especially be an issue during periods of financial stress, when the credit reliability of a fund family could be questioned.	92	9
201406	1284	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	It should also be noted that a government-only fund, while posing no credit risk, is likely to have a fixed NAV under the expected SEC proposal.	92	9
201406	1285	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	This could result in government funds being particularly attractive to hot money in times of financial stress, implying many of these funds may be faced with highly variable investor flows.	92	9
201406	1286	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thus, I am quite concerned that individual caps have collateral problems that are poorly understood at this time.	92	9
201406	1287	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would much prefer an aggregate cap.	92	9
201406	1288	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, I would set it at a much higher level than was discussed in the memo.	92	9
201406	1289	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	We want the cap to be binding during periods of significant stress, but we do not want it to be binding during normal periods, including the end of the quarter, the end of the year, and tax deadlines, when flows in and out of funds have the potential to be much larger than normal, particularly if this becomes an attractive vehicle for both corporate and retail investors.	92	9
201406	1290	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would set a large cap relative to our balance sheet that could be triggered only in quite stressful times.	92	9
201406	1291	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	The whole purpose of this facility is to tighten the spread under the short-term market rates relative to the rate of interest on reserves.	92	9
201406	1292	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	We want that to be binding unless there is significant financial instability, in which case the caps are binding, but we are also likely to be considering lowering significantly the reverse repo rate and, if it is likely to be of macroeconomic consequence, also the rate of interest on excess reserves.	92	9
201406	1293	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Question number 3—our taper strategy has been gradual, consistent, and transparent.	92	9
201406	1294	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Markets appear to have found this predictability reassuring.	92	9
201406	1295	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Rates and volatility have shown little reaction to our previous meetings’ decisions to taper our purchases.	92	9
201406	1296	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Learning from this experience, I would not make reinvestment discrete.	92	9
201406	1297	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Rather, I would, at the appropriate time, begin a somewhat symmetric taper of our reinvestments, reinvesting a percentage of principal repayments and reducing that percentage in a consistent and gradual way.	92	9
201406	1298	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	The hurdle for changing the tapering path for reinvestment would be similar to that for the current tapering program.	92	9
201406	1299	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	That is, we would continue on that path as long as we do not experience significant, unexpected changes to our economic forecast, either up or down.	92	9
201406	1300	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	In terms of when to start the reinvestment taper, I would make that dependent on the economic situation at the end of the year.	92	9
201406	1301	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	We might expect a diminished reinvestment around the time of our first rate increase, but we would move that forward in time if the economy is growing unexpectedly fast and put it back in time if the economy is disappointing.	92	9
201406	1302	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	For question 4, I am in favor of publishing an expanded benchmark as an additional benchmark rate.	92	9
201406	1303	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Until we have some experience with tightening rates, I would not use the current federal funds rate, or this additional benchmark, for anything other than informational purposes.	92	9
201406	1304	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	In summary, we should proceed cautiously and flexibly.	92	9
201406	1305	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	We should acknowledge that we are very likely to make changes as we learn from our initial actions.	92	9
201406	1306	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	We should not make any decisions about future operating procedures or what the eventual size of our balance sheet will be until we better understand the transition.	92	9
201406	1307	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	I expect that this facility will be successful and may become our future operating procedure.	92	9
201406	1308	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Allowing the short-term interest rate decision to be separate from the balance sheet decision gives us an important tool that we may want to use in the future.	92	9
201406	1309	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	In addition, there should be a broader discussion of our strategy in the context of financial stability.	92	9
201406	1310	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	For example, we may find value in keeping some MBS on the balance sheet, both for adjusting interest rates in some circumstances and for signaling in the event of another housing price bubble.	92	9
201406	1311	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Having some direct effect on long rates, as well as short rates, may be useful both for achieving our dual mandate and also for addressing financial-stability concerns, as our regulatory tools have long implementation lags and are cumbersome to use effectively.	92	9
201406	1312	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, I hope we continue to have an open mind until we better understand this facility.	92	9
201406	1313	2014-06-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1314	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you very much.	92	9
201406	1315	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	President Williams.	92	9
201406	1316	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1317	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Kudos, again, to the Board staff for comprehensive memos and presentations.	92	9
201406	1318	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Obviously, these questions have implications for monetary control, communications, and financial stability.	92	9
201406	1319	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	To begin, I just want to reiterate my support for the areas of common ground that are listed in exhibit 1 of the handout, especially, as President Rosengren mentioned himself, the need both for flexibility in our approach over the next few years and to recognize that we will be doing a lot of learning along this path.	92	9
201406	1320	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think we want to make sure we set up a plan that both allows for that flexibility and recognizes the need to learn along the way.	92	9
201406	1321	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	To preview my answers to the four questions, my preference is that we initially target a range for the federal funds rate.	92	9
201406	1322	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I believe that varying the interest rate on excess reserves and the reverse repo rate should be sufficient to achieve a reasonable target range—say, 25 basis points.	92	9
201406	1323	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	In terms of reverse repos and the need for caps, for financial-stability issues, I do think that aggregate quantity caps make sense as circuit breakers.	92	9
201406	1324	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I’d prefer these to be static rather than dynamic.	92	9
201406	1325	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	And I support delaying the end of reinvestments until sometime after liftoff.	92	9
201406	1326	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Finally, I am for having the New York Fed publish an expanded federal funds benchmark as a new rate, not as a substitute.	92	9
201406	1327	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	So let me expand on each of these points.	92	9
201406	1328	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	First, monetary control and financial stability both call for continuing to emphasize the fed funds rate during normalization.	92	9
201406	1329	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Most of the time, an administered overnight repo rate would provide similar monetary control of relevant short- term rates, but I do think targeting a market rate like the fed funds rate has an advantage, and that is that there can be times when there are idiosyncratic factors that drive the repo rate down or up, causing the spread from that repo rate to the market rate to be moved around.	92	9
201406	1330	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Going back to a principle from William Poole’s 1970 article in, targeting a market rate like the federal funds rate insulates you from idiosyncratic factors that create spreads between that and the repo rate and acts as an automatic stabilizer.	92	9
201406	1331	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	So that’s my argument for why a market rate is better than the overnight repo rate.	92	9
201406	1332	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	In terms of communications, our lengthy briefings and discussions on this issue make it clear that normalization is already complicated enough.	92	9
201406	1333	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	So, where possible, I think we’ve got to keep our procedures simple and familiar and make it easier for the public to understand our policies.	92	9
201406	1334	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	And as I said back in April, the fed funds rate may not be perfect, but it is well known.	92	9
201406	1335	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	So to the question of a point target versus a targeted range—I strongly support a range as we start this process of normalization.	92	9
201406	1336	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	A quarter-point range will provide sufficient macroeconomic control, while reducing pressure to immediately perfect our use of the IOER rate and the reverse repo facility.	92	9
201406	1337	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, over time we will learn how to best control the fed funds rate with these instruments.	92	9
201406	1338	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	We will also learn about how much take-up there will be on the overnight reverse repo facility.	92	9
201406	1339	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	And as we get that information, and we get a finer understanding of this, we can transition to a point target at some point in the future.	92	9
201406	1340	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	But to my mind, the most important thing we need to do in this early stage of normalization is to make sure that we can demonstrate to the public our confidence in our ability to control market interest rates per the requirements or per the desires or as needed for monetary policy goals.	92	9
201406	1341	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	In the early stages, I really see the need to focus attention on the fact that we have an interest rate we are trying to raise for macroeconomic reasons, and we are able to do it through the facilities we have.	92	9
201406	1342	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Turning to the second question, when it comes to circuit breakers on the overnight reverse repo facility, some sort of static cap would be simple and preferred.	92	9
201406	1343	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Dynamic caps are potentially subject to gaming and actually create some incentives for firms to use the facility more.	92	9
201406	1344	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	In addition, they are hard to properly calibrate, as said in some of the earlier conversations we had today, and I also think they are just more difficult to communicate.	92	9
201406	1345	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I recommend that we let the Committee adjust the cap as needed, as we learn more about the market take-up and behavior.	92	9
201406	1346	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Again, thinking of this as the early decision, it would be to have an aggregate fixed static cap, but then as we learn more over the next six months or a year after we start this process, we could adjust that.	92	9
201406	1347	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Third, I favor ending reinvestment sometime after liftoff.	92	9
201406	1348	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	My views on this are similar to how Governor Tarullo set up that question.	92	9
201406	1349	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Stopping reinvestment six months earlier or later should have negligible economic or financial effects.	92	9
201406	1350	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	This is just not a first-order policy decision in terms of the effects on the economic outlook and in terms of achievement of goals.	92	9
201406	1351	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	However, ending reinvestment before liftoff, or even at the time of liftoff, could be counterproductive because markets may see this, like they did last year, as a signal of a shift in direction toward much tighter policy by the Committee.	92	9
201406	1352	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I would rather avoid the problem of sending confusing signals by taking reinvestment off the table until we have the normalization of the funds rate well under way.	92	9
201406	1353	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	In a way, I think of this as wanting to get the reinvestment decision off the front page of the paper and buried in the back of the business section, because that really is the level of effect it has on the economy.	92	9
201406	1354	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	So I would not be more specific than that regarding the timing of the ending of reinvestment—there were some ideas of linking it to the interest rate or economic conditions.	92	9
201406	1355	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I do think we want to have that flexibility, for the reasons a number of people have already mentioned, to be able to make that decision based on economic conditions and financial conditions.	92	9
201406	1356	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	And when we do end reinvestment, we should keep it simple, and I would argue against trying to smooth the week-to-week or month-to-month reinvestment rates or trying to taper it.	92	9
201406	1357	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I actually think, again, this is not a first-order macro or financial event.	92	9
201406	1358	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think what we really need to do is just execute a plan.	92	9
201406	1359	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	One of the lessons I took—I guess we all take different lessons from events—was that once we started executing the taper, it went very smoothly.	92	9
201406	1360	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I don’t think that we really need to worry as much about market functioning around the ending of the reinvestment.	92	9
201406	1361	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Obviously, if there were real problems in market functioning, those should be taken into account.	92	9
201406	1362	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Fourth, I support publishing the expanded rate that includes Eurodollar transactions as an additional rate.	92	9
201406	1363	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	The rate on actual federal funds transactions, which would of course take advantage of the new FR-2420, would remain the basis of our communications, in my view.	92	9
201406	1364	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Focusing on fed funds transactions is simpler to communicate and should be fine for monetary control.	92	9
201406	1365	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	And the expanded rate might be more precise but offers limited benefits at this point in terms of our monetary policy target.	92	9
201406	1366	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	But, again, I am all for developing that.	92	9
201406	1367	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Let me finish up with some broader observations linked to some comments from the previous meeting and from President Kocherlakota and President Evans earlier about learning, language, and war-gaming.	92	9
201406	1368	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	We are going to learn a lot about this after we start this process.	92	9
201406	1369	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	So, again, I think we should start the normalization with familiar tools and terminology, wherever possible, and later changes then can be an evolution and not a reversal.	92	9
201406	1370	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Given that, the language we use in the revised exit principles should not lock us in unnecessarily.	92	9
201406	1371	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	For example, highlighting a range for the funds rate now would provide flexibility, and we can later narrow that range to a point, if it’s appropriate.	92	9
201406	1372	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	In terms of future statement language, draft 3', which provides a fed funds range, could be more explicit that the reverse repo facility supports the implementation of our federal funds rate target.	92	9
201406	1373	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	So rather than saying, “The Committee authorizes the Open Market Desk to execute overnight reverse repo agreements at a rate of 30 basis points,”	92	9
201406	1374	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I would prefer to say something like, “Consistent with this decision”—the decision about the federal funds rate target range—“the Committee authorizes the Open Market Desk to execute the reverse repo operations.”	92	9
201406	1375	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I do think a really open question is, where do we want this spread to be—and also, getting back to Governor Tarullo’s comments, how much take-up do we really want from this facility?	92	9
201406	1376	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Those, again, are things we will learn when we are actually doing it.	92	9
201406	1377	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Right now, we can maybe just guess.	92	9
201406	1378	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	And finally, as President Kocherlakota said in April, and as President Evans brought up, I do think we really need to think through or wargame some of these scenarios, and the scenarios that I think are more interesting are not like the fall of 2008.	92	9
201406	1379	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	In the fall of 2008, you’re cutting the funds rate to zero.	92	9
201406	1380	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	You’re driving all interest rates to zero.	92	9
201406	1381	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	That’s kind of a no-brainer from the point of view of thinking about some of these issues around market operations.	92	9
201406	1382	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	So you think more about a stress situation like in the Asian financial crisis and around that time, maybe even late 2007 and early 2008, when there were runs to safe assets but we actually had a target fed funds rate that was significantly above zero.	92	9
201406	1383	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	So then you start thinking about scenarios in which you are trying to maintain monetary policy control for dual-mandate reasons, at the same time that you are trying to deal with the fact that there is dislocation in the reverse repo or the Treasury market, and thinking about how these various arrangements and also how these caps could actually work.	92	9
201406	1384	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think that President Evans was pushing arguments along this line.	92	9
201406	1385	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	And I do think we should be thinking through those, and how we expect it would work, and to what extent we would need to have monetary policy decisions changing the interest rates in addition to the actual functioning of the facilities as set up.	92	9
201406	1386	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Obviously, the big question that has come up a number of times—President Kocherlakota brought it up at the previous meeting—is the credibility or the time-inconsistency of these caps.	92	9
201406	1387	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	In war-gaming this, we have to be realistic and think about how we would really behave in these stress scenarios, rather than what we would declare.	92	9
201406	1388	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think that this is something we should just continue to discuss and think about.	92	9
201406	1389	2014-06-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you very much.	92	9
201406	1390	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	President Kocherlakota.	92	9

201406	1399	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	If I may, Madam Chair, I’d first like to welcome two old friends to the Committee, Stan Fischer and Lael Brainard, and I suggest that we garnish Governor Fischer’s substantial new wages to pay me back for all the times he used the treadmill at the Hotel Okura and charged it to my room over in the—	92	9
201406	1400	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	[Laughter]	92	9

201406	1402	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	So I want to welcome both of you.	92	9
201406	1403	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	As I mentioned in the previous meeting, we are in the process of evolution.	92	9
201406	1404	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	I went back to Roosa, Volcker, Sternlight, Fisher, and now you, Simon Potter—obviously this discussion has informed this evolution enormously.	92	9
201406	1405	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	I found the previous meeting and this meeting, particularly the first parts of these meetings, to be enormously informative and very, very helpful, as well as the papers that were delivered, and I do want to give credit to everybody that prepared those papers and thank them for them.	92	9
201406	1406	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	But I do think we need to proceed deliberately, and I’m going to answer the questions with that in mind, bearing in mind again, as I mentioned earlier, that unlike in the old days, we in essence are only one-quarter or maybe one-fifth of the credit system, and we have to be mindful of that fact as we process these different questions.	92	9
201406	1407	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	I was captivated by and am in full agreement with Governor Tarullo’s statement and also, shockingly, increasingly over time thinking more and more like President Rosengren.	92	9
201406	1408	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	But to start out with question 1, I do think we ought to use the IOER rate as the principal tool to affect interest rates.	92	9
201406	1409	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	I have a concern about the ON RRP program.	92	9
201406	1410	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	I want to talk about that in just a second, but I do think that basically the principal tool to affect interest rates is the IOER rate.	92	9
201406	1411	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	With regard to the ON RRP program, I was affected by the discussion we had today about using it as a circuit breaker.	92	9
201406	1412	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	I think that makes eminent sense.	92	9
201406	1413	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	I have concerns, however—and I hope the New York Desk will forgive me—I don’t mean this critically, but when, for example, we looked at exhibit 4, item number 22, and you mentioned your option was to add more counterparties of the current types, there’s a little bit of a “more the merrier” tune that comes through the memo that was written in terms of the review of the counterparty framework for overnight RRP operations, and I think we have to be careful here.	92	9
201406	1414	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	I think there ought to be a clear and principled dividing line between those with access to that facility and those without.	92	9
201406	1415	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	We could discuss what that dividing line should be.	92	9
201406	1416	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	My concern, Madam Chair, is that—and maybe this is what Governor Tarullo was saying—I don’t have a sense of final dimension here.	92	9
201406	1417	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	And I’m worried, given the fact that there are so many possible counterparties, and given the fact that we’re one-quarter or one-fifth of the credit system, that this could grow like Topsy and maybe grow slightly out of control.	92	9
201406	1418	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	We can’t be all things to all people, and we have to figure out what the strict limitations and definitions are.	92	9
201406	1419	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	I’m not saying we should not have RRP operations, but I personally struggle with what the order of dimension will be.	92	9
201406	1420	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	I could make a case that, if we had a clear and principled dividing line, we would include depository institutions—our traditional Fed partners—the Federal Home Loan Banks, the housing GSEs, and government money market funds.	92	9
201406	1421	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	I could make a case for excluding the prime money market funds.	92	9
201406	1422	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	But I am a little bit worried that if we just keep adding more, we might create something that puts us in a place of being too much a part of the market, and I just wanted to voice that honestly and frankly to the Desk and to the rest of the folks at the table.	92	9
201406	1423	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	With regard to the issue of reinvestment of principal, I think President Rosengren makes a very good point.	92	9
201406	1424	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	I view that as a signaling device, and as much as we want to define forward guidance with specificity, as much as we try to define an exit principle with great specificity, as President Rosengren pointed out, we’ve had two goes at it before.	92	9
201406	1425	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	This is very much a matter of feel.	92	9
201406	1426	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	The term “war-gaming” has been used quite a bit in today’s discussion.	92	9
201406	1427	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	The old way to conduct a war is, you didn’t shoot until you saw the whites of the eyes of your opponents.	92	9
201406	1428	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	With modern technology and modern modeling and so on, that’s been affected, but I mention that only because I would feel comfortable moving the base rate up once we see the whites of the eyes of a full recovery and meeting the dual mandate.	92	9
201406	1429	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	There may be a utility in using the reinvestment tool as we feel more confident, but don’t quite have the absolute level of confidence we would need to raise the base rate, depending on how the economy evolves, as President Rosengren said.	92	9
201406	1430	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	I don’t think it makes a huge difference in terms of affecting the size of the balance sheet, but it is a signaling device.	92	9
201406	1431	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	I would be in favor of keeping open the option of tapering back our repurchases—I think, President Rosengren, you used the phrase “symmetric reduction”—in order to send a signal to the market that we’re increasingly confident and it’s a bridge to raising the base rate.	92	9
201406	1432	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	Because the other thing I feel very strongly about, and I’ve discussed this with you offline, Madam Chair, is that when we decide to raise the base rate, I don’t want to do things in a sudden, old-fashioned way.	92	9
201406	1433	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	I’d like to do it by a quarter-point or maybe less than a quarter-point at a time.	92	9
201406	1434	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	So those are my feelings on the reinvestment of principal.	92	9
201406	1435	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	As to the fourth point, I am in favor of continuing to publish something very much like the current funds rate, but maybe described as the overnight bank funding rate that would capture trades in the overnight Eurodollar market.	92	9
201406	1436	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	We had a little discussion there, clarified and then confused by our great legal counsel, but I’m basically arguing the case that option 1 might be the easiest thing to do from the standpoint of the transactional commitments that exist in the marketplace.	92	9
201406	1437	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	And I think one of the benefits of that would be that limiting to domestic institutions and US offices of foreign institutions could blunt the political criticism we might receive if there was a sense that we were providing a facility that’s unduly influenced by foreign borrowing costs.	92	9
201406	1438	2014-06-18	meeting	FISHER	Those are my overall views, Madam Chair, and I realize they’re not all that specific, but we’re still feeling our way through this, and we’ll get more specific as we go through time.	92	9

201406	1453	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1454	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	The discussion so far has been useful and illuminating.	92	9
201406	1455	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	There are many complexities and subtleties, and when presented with a number of tradeoffs in which the choice isn’t clear-cut, my approach is to pose some framing questions or tests as a way to sort through the options.	92	9
201406	1456	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	My tests are, first, the probability of achieving control over short-term rates; second, where feasible, some flexibility to allow tactical adaptation as we learn; and, third, simplicity and clarity of communications.	92	9
201406	1457	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	When I go through the questions I will reorder them a little bit and bunch some together.	92	9
201406	1458	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	On the question of the emphasis on the federal funds rate or administered rates, first, I expect we’re going to settle on using alternate rates for both monetary control and communications purposes, and I think it’s worth trying to preserve in that construct the use of the fed funds rate.	92	9
201406	1459	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I favor beginning with a target range for the federal funds rate, since it is now familiar and probably more workable in the early stages.	92	9
201406	1460	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	So I favor the second of the two options presented in the staff memo.	92	9
201406	1461	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I see it as giving us the best chance of exerting control over short-term rates.	92	9
201406	1462	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	If we go this way, a first order of business will be to construct statements that are as clear as possible, given all the moving parts.	92	9
201406	1463	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I think the 3' verbiage in the illustrative time of liftoff statement would meet the test of clarity and simplicity.	92	9
201406	1464	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Now I’ll go to question 4, and that is the question about publishing an expanded fed funds rate definition.	92	9
201406	1465	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I’m open to an expanded federal funds rate, including an expansion that incorporates Eurodollar transactions, along with nonbrokered fed funds transactions.	92	9
201406	1466	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	At the same time I think we should aim for the most durable definition possible of the target funds rate, and that leads me to thinking that we should include in our planning the scenario in which we return to a balance sheet of a size at which reserves are relatively scarce.	92	9
201406	1467	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	So I don’t know if including Eurodollar transactions presents any issue in such a scenario, and this is the kind of question I think we can sort out in coming deliberations.	92	9
201406	1468	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	On question 2, about circuit breakers—I thought the staff took a mostly neutral position in the presentation of options in the memos, but on this question I thought the staff went pretty far in pushing a cap on aggregate usage paired with a uniform-price auction mechanism.	92	9
201406	1469	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I think this is a sensible place to start.	92	9
201406	1470	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Although this is perhaps not a decisive consideration, this approach strikes me as simpler and less problematic to implement in terms of IT systems adjustments, as was pointed out in the memo.	92	9
201406	1471	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Some of my other duties in the System make me attentive to such a statement.	92	9
201406	1472	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I’d like to spend more time on this question of limits and circuit breakers leading up to the July decision point, and I hope we can ask follow-up questions of the staff during the period before the next meeting.	92	9
201406	1473	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	The third question, which I’ll treat as the last one, is the reinvestment question—ceasing reinvestments or taking a graduated approach.	92	9
201406	1474	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Ending reinvestments simultaneously or coincident with liftoff is clearest and conveys greater conviction, but I’m open to doing it after liftoff because I think this buys some time to observe how the first phase of tightening goes.	92	9
201406	1475	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I think the reinvestment program can be ended or wound down based on tactical considerations after the transition represented by liftoff has been accomplished.	92	9
201406	1476	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	This, I think, is an area in which tactical flexibility is feasible.	92	9
201406	1477	2014-06-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9

201406	1491	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	So I want to thank them for all that.	92	9
201406	1492	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I don’t want to upset Governor Tarullo, but I’m afraid—	92	9
201406	1493	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Nobody wants to.	92	9
201406	1494	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I’m afraid I’m going to have to agree with a lot of he said.	92	9
201406	1495	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	[Laughter]	92	9
201406	1496	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	Now, if that forces him to recant all that—I hope not, but I actually share a lot of his views, as you’ll see in my remarks.	92	9
201406	1497	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	But before I address the specific questions under consideration, I’d like to state some of my general views regarding the normalization of policy.	92	9
201406	1498	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	It appears to me that a lot of our discussion recently about our exit and normalization are overly concerned with the daily volatility in overnight rates.	92	9
201406	1499	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I’m a bit uncomfortable with the extent to which these concerns are driving our policy options.	92	9
201406	1500	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	Historically, volatility in the funds rate has always been an operational feature of monetary policy, and I see no compelling reason why we can’t continue to accept volatility or why we should expect that that volatility will impede our ability to carry out policy consistent with our broad macroeconomic mandate.	92	9
201406	1501	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	Also, I’m reluctant to move to conducting monetary policy operations with a large set of nonbank counterparties and to essentially sidestep the legal restriction on paying interest on reserves to anyone that is not a depository institution.	92	9
201406	1502	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I fear doing so could potentially have some unpleasant political ramifications.	92	9
201406	1503	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I also want to restate my guiding principle that any near-term tactical decisions we make should leave open the option of returning to a corridor system of some kind based on the fed funds rate or perhaps a more broadly defined interbank rate sometime in the future, which is my preferred way of conducting policy.	92	9
201406	1504	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	This means I probably would not support any communication or tactical steps that suggest we prefer or will rely on other instruments to administer monetary policy on a regular or routine basis.	92	9
201406	1505	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	Special facilities, such as the TDF or the overnight reverse repo facility, should be viewed and communicated as temporary and shelved when not absolutely necessary.	92	9
201406	1506	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	With that in mind, in the interim as we shrink the balance sheet, I would rely primarily on the IOER administered rate, but then I would specify a range for the funds rate as we’ve been doing for the past five years.	92	9
201406	1507	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	It’s not new anymore.	92	9
201406	1508	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	In doing that, I would be inclined and even comfortable if we expanded the range of that federal funds rate—maybe it doesn’t need to be 20 or 25 basis points.	92	9
201406	1509	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	Maybe it can be 40 basis points.	92	9
201406	1510	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	We can have a broad range initially.	92	9
201406	1511	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	And then we may indicate that we would use other tools at our disposal—intentionally vague there—in the short run to ensure that the federal funds rate or our expanded definition doesn’t fall below that broad range.	92	9
201406	1512	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	That would keep the ON RRP a smaller facility, at least in the near term.	92	9
201406	1513	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	As we gain more experience, we will find out if that works, and whether we need to employ the ON RRP rate to keep the funds rate in its target range.	92	9
201406	1514	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	As we raise rates, we might be able to shrink the funds rate target range as we get more comfortable with our ability to conduct monetary policy by having the IOER rate raise rates.	92	9
201406	1515	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	As I said, I would also be comfortable with expanding or extending the definition of the effective funds rate to include Eurodollar transactions.	92	9
201406	1516	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I’ll note that, in exhibit 20 from the briefing we had this morning, if you look at the period between 2010 and 2014 when there was a lot of volatility, the Eurodollar rate and the fed funds rate moved around pretty close together.	92	9
201406	1517	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	There doesn’t seem to be a huge disconnect between these two markets, so I’m comfortable expanding the definition of the fed funds rate in that dimension.	92	9
201406	1518	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I think proceeding along these lines will make it easy for us to return to our corridor system that targets the domestic interbank rate.	92	9
201406	1519	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I’d also note that as a governance matter, the FOMC and the Board of Governors would need to articulate a shared understanding of how the IOER rate would be set, and how that would be set relative to the funds rate range, until such a time as we can return to an explicit funds rate target.	92	9
201406	1520	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	So I prefer this option to targeting the ON RRP rate specifically.	92	9
201406	1521	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I believe that relying on the ON RRP rate is risky.	92	9
201406	1522	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	We do not know the consequences for the microeconomic structure of short-term funding markets, or who’s being helped or harmed by us crowding into this market in such a big way.	92	9
201406	1523	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	We are already witnessing an increase in demand from many people who wish to be counterparties.	92	9
201406	1524	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	Why is that?	92	9
201406	1525	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I don’t suspect they’re doing it out of patriotism.	92	9
201406	1526	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I suspect there’s a financial reason why they’d like to do that.	92	9
201406	1527	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	So there must be financial benefits to this, and we could be artificially creating or at least in some sense encouraging a huge demand for this product.	92	9
201406	1528	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	But who are we squeezing out, and what will the consequences of that be, both intended and unintended?	92	9
201406	1529	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	And what does this have to do with operating monetary policy and achieving our macroeconomic goals?	92	9
201406	1530	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	As I previously mentioned, I’m very uncomfortable with the fact that we are engaging, I think, in a backdoor practice of paying interest on reserves to nondepository institutions.	92	9
201406	1531	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	Governor Tarullo made a pretty articulate argument about the financial-stability risks and implications of this facility.	92	9
201406	1532	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	We don’t know a lot about how it will play out, but I don’t think we ought to be designing our monetary policy instruments and operating procedures and using a monetary policy instrument for financial-stability reasons—I think we’re conflating those two.	92	9
201406	1533	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	Even today I heard people moving back and forth between the ON RRP facility as a tool for monetary policy and as a tool to meet liquidity needs in the case of a crisis.	92	9
201406	1534	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I think we should be very careful about that.	92	9
201406	1535	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	So with respect to question 2, as I said, I am opposed to a full-allotment program for reverse repos.	92	9
201406	1536	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	If we choose to use reverse repos at all as a tactical tool during a transition to a smaller balance sheet, I prefer fewer counterparties and probably aggregate caps.	92	9
201406	1537	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	The size of the cap should be an FOMC decision.	92	9
201406	1538	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	Simplicity would be desirable, and thus, probably, I would start with an aggregate cap that’s static rather than one that’s dynamic.	92	9
201406	1539	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I think our communications are hard enough without explaining how we’re going to dynamically adjust some kind of cap.	92	9
201406	1540	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I do not like the fact that the overnight reverse repo facility seems to be making it convenient for some institutions to dress up their balance sheets at the end of the quarter.	92	9
201406	1541	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I don’t see that as a macroeconomic goal or role for the Federal Reserve, but this facility seems to be providing great support for at least some institutions to do that.	92	9
201406	1542	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	That gives me pause to think about whether or not a counterparty cap might be appropriate as well, and I’m open to thinking further about that.	92	9
201406	1543	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	Again, simplicity, I think, is going to be valuable.	92	9
201406	1544	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I would urge us to go in a different direction.	92	9
201406	1545	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I would urge us to play down the role of the ON RRP facility as much as we can.	92	9
201406	1546	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	It is a transitional facility that we will use as the balance sheet shrinks, but not in an ongoing way.	92	9
201406	1547	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	Like President Rosengren, I think it is a bit awkward at best for us to be entertaining an operating system in which money market funds are the major transmitter of monetary policy, particularly given our concerns that we have expressed both within the Committee and more publicly about the financial-stability issues surrounding money market funds.	92	9
201406	1548	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	That does suggest to me that shrinking the counterparties may be the right approach—and I’d be willing to think about this further—just considering government-only money market funds as counterparties if we choose to go in that direction.	92	9
201406	1549	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	Regarding question 3, I am in favor of terminating our reinvestments in a prompt manner after the taper has ended.	92	9
201406	1550	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	As many people have mentioned, the process of reducing or tapering our purchases, once we told the markets what we were going to do, has come off pretty smoothly, and I would be inclined just to keep on going.	92	9
201406	1551	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	We’re tapering slowly.	92	9
201406	1552	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	We can continue to taper and shrink the balance sheet, and I would be open to that—in fact, I even would encourage it.	92	9
201406	1553	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I’d also like to see some more discussion concerning the desirability of changing the maturity structure of the balance sheet.	92	9
201406	1554	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	We have a highly mismatched balance sheet subject to political risk, I think, as well as credit risk of various kinds.	92	9
201406	1555	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	And as some people have argued, we are in the midst of a very large carry trade right now, and we’re going to have to unwind that at some point, and there will be costs to bear when we do that.	92	9
201406	1556	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I’ll have some more to say about this later, but one thing that we might consider as we think about reinvestment is maybe we ought to be shifting our reinvestments into short-term Treasuries that would allow us a little more flexibility on our balance sheet as we move forward in time.	92	9
201406	1557	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	That might be a step to manage our balance sheet’s maturity structure and exit.	92	9
201406	1558	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	Finally, let me reiterate that I’m supportive of extending the definition of the interbank rate that we target.	92	9
201406	1559	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	The funds rate and the Eurodollar rate seem to move pretty closely together.	92	9
201406	1560	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	And I would encourage the staff to do some more work and give us some more data on these rates that go back a little further in time.	92	9
201406	1561	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	I think it may enhance our ability to conduct monetary policy in the future.	92	9
201406	1562	2014-06-18	meeting	PLOSSER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
