201406	1564	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	President Evans.	92	9
201406	1565	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1566	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	And thanks to the staff for excellent analysis of complex financial products and financial engineering of some of these tools.	92	9
201406	1567	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	I agree with the staff’s overview assessment of the Committee’s consensus position from April.	92	9
201406	1568	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	When it becomes appropriate to reduce monetary accommodation, the Committee expects to employ our IOER and overnight RRP tools with a relatively wide spread between them, so that federal funds rate can be expected to trade within an indicated range.	92	9
201406	1569	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	As long as our balance sheet remains larger than in our prior policy environment, circa 2007, using the overnight RRP tool to firm up short-term money rates is a useful approach.	92	9
201406	1570	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	That said, I do not favor moving to a floor system for the longer term.	92	9
201406	1571	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	And even if we did, I would not favor a permanent ON RRP program, for reasons that I will expand upon shortly.	92	9
201406	1572	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	So I think it is crucial that the language announcing our use of the ON RRP program and our exit strategy should emphasize the temporary duration of this policy tool.	92	9
201406	1573	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	We should be explicit about the temporary nature of our use of ON RRPs during our policy normalization period.	92	9
201406	1574	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Otherwise, market participants will assume it is here for good and make costly market structure investments.	92	9
201406	1575	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	At that point, we will almost surely accept that our credibility will require us to maintain the overnight RRP program indefinitely.	92	9
201406	1576	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	In order to avoid this eventual and unplanned fait accompli outcome, we need to be explicit, now and throughout the program’s use, that this is a temporary facility.	92	9
201406	1577	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Let me be clear: I worry about the complexity of this market, and I would prefer not using it at all, if that were reasonable.	92	9
201406	1578	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Over the transition period, while we renormalize our policy settings, the overnight program can be an insurance policy that helps us to hit a target for the funds rate, and that is an important benefit.	92	9
201406	1579	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	As long as we take prudent actions to minimize financial instability risks over this transition period, I can see some benefits to using the program temporarily.	92	9
201406	1580	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	But over the longer term, I don’t see the benefits, certainly not relative to the possibly large costs of increased financial instability.	92	9
201406	1581	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	If anyone thinks there is a big payoff to having a permanent overnight RRP program, now is the time to provide that important quantitative and persuasive analysis.	92	9
201406	1582	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Maybe I’m overly risk averse, and there are actually important benefits.	92	9
201406	1583	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	But I think a compelling affirmative case still needs to be made for this program to be used permanently.	92	9
201406	1584	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	As the briefing memos discuss, there is a potential for the overnight RRP program to generate financial instability problems.	92	9
201406	1585	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	For example, during a period of heightened risk aversion, a full-allotment program could lead to destabilizing withdrawals of funding from money funds and other lending institutions to avoid exposure to credit instruments with even modest credit risk.	92	9
201406	1586	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	To address these risks, the memos discussed aggregate caps, individual caps, dynamic and flexible caps, and other circuit breakers.	92	9
201406	1587	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	These discussions did an unusually good job of convincing me that this new financial instrument is much too complicated.	92	9
201406	1588	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	We just don’t know how it’s going to interact with other short-term funding markets during times of stress.	92	9
201406	1589	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	For a temporary implementation of this program, I would favor an aggregate static cap for simplicity.	92	9
201406	1590	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Before we find ourselves endgamed with a permanent overnight RRP instrument for monetary policy, we simply need more analysis of how such an interest rate tool would affect our policy effectiveness during normal times under various stress scenarios—that is, during normal times when the funds rate is 4 percent or more, but we face a stress scenario.	92	9
201406	1591	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Obviously, I am focusing a lot of my attention on the possibility that this program will be around 5 or 10 years from now.	92	9
201406	1592	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	My misgivings mean that I have to know one heck of a lot more about the effectiveness of this new policy tool, its social value, and its use as a new financial product before I can imagine undertaking actions today that would likely lead to it becoming a permanent operational fixture.	92	9
201406	1593	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	In the absence of a strong and compelling case for a longer-term floor system, I favor only a temporary use of this program.	92	9
201406	1594	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	At the time we invoke our normalization strategy, we should authorize its use either for one year or until a date in the future when we estimate our SOMA balance sheet will approximately return to normal, and no longer than that.	92	9
201406	1595	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Now, let me turn to reinvestments.	92	9
201406	1596	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	I prefer changing our strategy so that we continue reinvesting maturing proceeds until well after we begin our interest rate tightening.	92	9
201406	1597	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Given the long duration of our SOMA portfolio, I don’t believe there is a material change in the degree of accommodation that is provided under the various timing possibilities for reinvestments.	92	9
201406	1598	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	I think signaling our policy intentions is simpler and cleaner if we reduce the list of policy watch variables to just the interest rate liftoff decision itself.	92	9
201406	1599	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Putting this all together for the sake of being clear about my preferred approach, here is how I could see the FOMC policy statement emerging.	92	9
201406	1600	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Key ingredients are found in paragraph 3 of the illustrative liftoff policy statement example in the planning memo.	92	9
201406	1601	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	At the appropriate time, I would state that the Committee decided to increase its target funds rate to 0.25 percent.	92	9
201406	1602	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	But due to large excess reserves during our extended policy normalization period, the effective funds rate may range from 15 to 40 basis points, perhaps.	92	9
201406	1603	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	So this is like paragraph 3 but with a target federal funds rate and an expected trading range.	92	9
201406	1604	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Basically, we announce the target funds rate, and we admit upfront that during the normalization process trading may occur in the range around the target.	92	9
201406	1605	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Now, I have heard all the conversation so far, and it strikes me that a range is what is going to be the consensus for the funds rate.	92	9
201406	1606	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	So that is okay.	92	9
201406	1607	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	In this case, I am okay with using the existing language in paragraph 3 on the Committee authorizing the overnight RRP rate to be within a range of 15 to 25 basis points and setting the IOER rate to 40 basis points.	92	9
201406	1608	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	However, I would hope that IOER alone could do most of the tightening work for us, and I would favor starting out with the overnight RRP rate at 15 basis points and not being that anxious to increase it if the funds rate trades a little below 25 basis points.	92	9
201406	1609	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Of course, if the funds rate was persistently far below 25 basis points, we could raise the overnight rate somewhat.	92	9
201406	1610	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Let me add that I have not come to a firm view about whether we should target an expanded version of the funds rate that includes Eurodollars.	92	9
201406	1611	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	I am open to arguments from the technical experts.	92	9
201406	1612	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Finally, let me conclude by saying that I think it’s obvious that engineering a smooth increase in short-term policy rates with our enormous balance sheet will be fraught with temporary obstacles and challenges.	92	9
201406	1613	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	I think we need to be very explicit in accepting that at various times we will see markets both overreact and underreact to our policy-tightening moves.	92	9
201406	1614	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	It’s going to happen.	92	9
201406	1615	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Let’s not compound the challenges of our task with an unrealistic expectation that policy adjustment will go 100 percent as we draw it up on the board.	92	9
201406	1616	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Let’s deal with the known unknowns as best we can and react as prudently as possible when the unknown unknowns arise.	92	9
201406	1617	2014-06-18	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1618	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201406	1619	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Powell.	92	9
201406	1620	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1621	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I generally support what the Chair referred to at the outset as the centrist approach for liftoff and for the early stages of normalization, of managing short-term rates with IOER pulling up from above and the ON RRP facility available to provide a floor and push up from below, if needed.	92	9
201406	1622	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Today, IOER is at 25 basis points, federal funds are trading around 10 basis points, and the ON RRP rate is set at 5 basis points.	92	9
201406	1623	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	So this really just means moving the whole structure upward as the Committee tightens policy, and it ought to give the Committee a reasonable level of control over short-term rates.	92	9
201406	1624	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Of course, that remains to be seen.	92	9
201406	1625	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	It also seems likely—and I take it as a given for purposes of this discussion—that the Committee will support development of an improved measure for the federal funds rate based on the FR-2420 data and including Eurodollar transactions.	92	9
201406	1626	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	And I assume—I had assumed, anyway—that if we go to the trouble of creating this rate, and then choose to target a federal funds rate, that is the one we would target.	92	9
201406	1627	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I would find it odd that we would do all the work to create this thing and put it out there and then not have the confidence to target it, but instead target the old one.	92	9
201406	1628	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I’m not sure how we would explain that.	92	9
201406	1629	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	So that’s going to be my assumption for this purpose.	92	9
201406	1630	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I also have to say that I share the discomfort with the potential for the RRP facility to get very large very quickly.	92	9
201406	1631	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	For me, the facility is just a tool to provide a floor for rates, and it need not be a perfect floor.	92	9
201406	1632	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Nothing more.	92	9
201406	1633	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	As I said at the last meeting, I have been thinking that it could be small and tailored for that limited purpose.	92	9
201406	1634	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Really, though, the question that has been raised is, is that possible?	92	9
201406	1635	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	If you go back to what’s discussed in the memo, a facility that is sized off a trailing one-week average of usage volume with a $300 billion cushion could grow enormously very quickly, obviously.	92	9
201406	1636	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	And even if you lengthened the averaging period and lowered the surge capacity, it still could get very large, and the effect on industry structures would be unpredictable at best.	92	9
201406	1637	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I also don’t know that there is any real answer to the fact that the caps would come under huge pressure in a crisis—I would characterize them as speed bumps, others have called them circuit breakers—and that the market will see that in advance and plan on it.	92	9
201406	1638	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	So I have those concerns, and from the standpoint of the counterparties, I would prefer to choose the first option, which is to say, let’s wait to make decisions about counterparties until there is significantly more discussion on how we can create an ON RRP facility that will do what we need it to do, but not threaten to become something that we really don’t want—that I don’t want, let’s say.	92	9
201406	1639	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Within that general framework, with a role for IOER, for the federal funds rate, and for the ON RRP facility, there are some choices to be made, and the first is whether to target the improved federal funds rate as either a point or a range or, instead, to target short-term rates.	92	9
201406	1640	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	"The options are there in paragraphs 3, 3', and 3"", and—no surprise—my desire would be to use the ON RRP facility only as needed, and that pushes me in the direction of 3'."	92	9
201406	1641	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I would echo what President Evans was perhaps suggesting, though—that a point target with expected volatility around it kind of approaches a range in the limit.	92	9
201406	1642	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	And also, in these formulations, in 3 and 3', the communication is around the federal funds rate, and the tools are there as supporting characters.	92	9
201406	1643	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	"In option 3"", the communication is very different and is really focused on the administered rates, and the general level of short-term rates, including the federal funds rate, is kind of an afterthought."	92	9
201406	1644	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Let me say that I find it a plausible idea to target the general level of short-term rates including the federal funds rate, but I don’t like the idea of featuring the administered rates as the primary actors in the play, if you will.	92	9
201406	1645	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	And I would say that I do like the idea of thinking of IOER as the principal tool.	92	9
201406	1646	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	The second issue is whether to continue to publish the old federal funds rate alongside the new and improved version or to just publish the improved version and call it the federal funds rate, and take the old federal funds rate off the market, put it out to pasture—pick your metaphor—but have it out there in case we need it later.	92	9
201406	1647	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	My preference is what I would call the one-rate solution, which is to publish the new rate and call it the federal funds rate.	92	9
201406	1648	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	The work of the LIBOR reform effort covers some of these same issues, and maybe it can shed some light by analogy.	92	9
201406	1649	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	The LIBOR reform effort has included a Market Participants Group established by the Official Sector Steering Committee (OSSC) of the FSB and led by Darrell Duffie, a well-known academic, and it included financial market participants of all different varieties.	92	9
201406	1650	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Noting the current state of play in the federal funds market, the Market Participants Group said that “it would hesitate to recommend the federal funds rate as a reference rate without an improved fixing.”	92	9
201406	1651	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	And one critical test that the federal funds rate is at risk of not meeting the standards for a reference rate is that principle 7 of the IOSCO benchmark principles requires that a benchmark be anchored in real transactions in an active market.	92	9
201406	1652	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	In addition, the LIBOR Market Participants Group recommended—and the OSSC agrees—that the definition of LIBOR should be broadened to include a wider range of transactions and counterparties, and that it be anchored in real transactions.	92	9
201406	1653	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	And this is kind of a direct parallel to federal funds reform.	92	9
201406	1654	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Market participants did not prefer an option that kept the old LIBOR alive and created a new rate with these improved characteristics.	92	9
201406	1655	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Instead, they preferred a rate that is called LIBOR, but that is no longer limited to London or to interbank lending, and it’s not an offered rate either [laughter] but, rather, is anchored in real transactions.	92	9
201406	1656	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I don’t say this is dispositive, but it suggests to me that market participants have concerns about the federal funds rate as a reliable benchmark and would probably like to see it reformed, which I believe would mean changing the definition of the federal funds rate, rather than creating a new rate and naming it something else.	92	9
201406	1657	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	In addition, I don’t really think it’s less confusing or easier for market participants to have two rates out there.	92	9
201406	1658	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I don’t know how you explain that.	92	9
201406	1659	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	It’s just a level of complexity that I don’t think we need.	92	9
201406	1660	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	The other issue we talked about earlier is the contract frustration issue, which, as I mentioned, I don’t see as a serious concern and shouldn’t be the thing that pushes us around in this issue.	92	9
201406	1661	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	So where that leaves me is, I favor one rate to be called the federal funds rate.	92	9
201406	1662	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	It will include Eurodollars and the FR-2420 transactions.	92	9
201406	1663	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Turning to the second question from the appendix, as I mentioned, I’m less sure that circuit breakers can be successful in limiting the size and effect of the facility over time.	92	9
201406	1664	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	But, nonetheless, this is how I would make the tradeoffs.	92	9
201406	1665	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I’d like an aggregate cap with a single-price auction to allocate capacity if the cap is hit.	92	9
201406	1666	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I’d like that cap to be rigid.	92	9
201406	1667	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I think I’d like it to be static.	92	9
201406	1668	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I’d like X, which is to say the surge capacity, to be low—no more than $50 billion.	92	9
201406	1669	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	And I would allow indulgences for quarter-end and other scheduled events like that.	92	9
201406	1670	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I don’t think I would see those as reasons to trip the surge capacity.	92	9
201406	1671	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I would look more for changes in capacity.	92	9
201406	1672	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Finally, moving to reinvestment, I’ve got several concerns about ceasing reinvestments soon after the taper ends.	92	9
201406	1673	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	First, I think this could correctly be seen as the beginning of tightening, and there is a risk of a market reaction that might actually have the effect of pushing out the liftoff date.	92	9
201406	1674	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Now, I don’t know that, but let me say that after the last two major decisions it is very hard for me to feel like I have a lot of confidence in predicting how the market would take this signal.	92	9
201406	1675	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	If you look back to, for example, the June meeting last year, I think people pretty widely underestimated the market reaction.	92	9
201406	1676	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Then comes the actual taper at the end of the year, and I will say I overestimated what would happen.	92	9
201406	1677	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I think that taper was clearly well justified on the economics, but not at all expected by the market.	92	9
201406	1678	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	But who thought that the stock market would close up 300 points?	92	9
201406	1679	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	So, I would say, same lesson, different sign, in both cases.	92	9
201406	1680	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	But in any case, there is the possibility of a market reaction that might push out the liftoff date.	92	9
201406	1681	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Second, even if that doesn’t happen, to me the highest priority when it is time to tighten policy is to get away from the effective lower bound.	92	9
201406	1682	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	And so for any given amount of tightening, using both tools by definition means that we’ll be raising rates less.	92	9
201406	1683	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Third, I think that using both tools at the same time can be confusing.	92	9
201406	1684	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	And, finally, I am concerned that terminating our reinvestments in MBS, which amount to a substantial part of projected gross issuance, could well flow through into higher mortgage rates, albeit probably at a modest amount, and I just don’t think that higher mortgage rates are what we need right now in the economy.	92	9
201406	1685	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	For that reason, I am open to the idea of smoothing the taper.	92	9
201406	1686	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I also think that the idea of creating an agreed path for the taper is a good one.	92	9
201406	1687	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	I don’t know that I have a great answer on that one.	92	9
201406	1688	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Finally, I would prefer to stop reinvestments well after liftoff, and I would avoid hard and complex triggers.	92	9
201406	1689	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	One approach would be to state an intention to hold the balance sheet stable at least until the target rate is, for example, 1 percent, which feels like about the end of 2015 in that case.	92	9
201406	1690	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Or you could take a softer approach and defer to Committee judgment as to when is the appropriate time.	92	9
201406	1691	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	But I do think it would be helpful to take it off the table for now, focus on raising rates and getting away from the zero lower bound, and return to it near the end of 2015.	92	9
201406	1692	2014-06-18	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1693	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201406	1694	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Vice Chairman.	92	9
201406	1695	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1696	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	It’s probably appropriate for me to begin with the issue of reinvestment.	92	9
201406	1697	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	As I noted in a speech last month, I think there are some compelling reasons for ending reinvestments sometime after liftoff of short-term rates rather than before or coincident with liftoff.	92	9
201406	1698	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	In my mind, ending reinvestments later, after liftoff, serves four purposes.	92	9
201406	1699	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	First, it lessens the risk of foreshortening the entire tightening process.	92	9
201406	1700	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	If we were to end reinvestments before liftoff, then the end of reinvestments would be viewed as the beginning of the tightening process.	92	9
201406	1701	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	That runs the risk of both raising long-term rates, especially to the extent that people emphasize flows rather than stocks, and also raising the expected trajectory of short-term rates because it would pull forward people’s expectations in terms of the probability of liftoff, and the timing of liftoff would be pulled forward in time.	92	9
201406	1702	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Thus, I think ending reinvestments first could lead to a significant tightening of financial conditions that might be more than we desire or anticipate.	92	9
201406	1703	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	That could disrupt the economic expansion, and that could actually delay the liftoff of short-term interest rates.	92	9
201406	1704	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Similarly, if we end reinvestment and commence liftoff together, the effect could be greater than we anticipate, and if it was greater than we desired, it might be awkward, if we’re doing both together, to then reverse course.	92	9
201406	1705	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I also think separating the two decisions reduces the risk of an overly-large market response.	92	9
201406	1706	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Second, because ending reinvestments first could conceivably delay liftoff in certain states of the world, it is inconsistent with our goal of getting off the zero lower bound as soon as possible in order to regain monetary policy flexibility.	92	9
201406	1707	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	It seems to me that getting off the zero lower bound as soon as possible, consistent with our dual-mandate objectives, should be a goal of policy, as that would provide greater flexibility in terms of responding to future shocks.	92	9
201406	1708	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Third, I think delaying the end of reinvestments also should simplify our communications as we lift off.	92	9
201406	1709	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	There will be one moving part—short-term interest rates—rather than two.	92	9
201406	1710	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Also, if we’re adjusting both short-term rates and the size of the balance sheet at the same time, I think it would be more difficult for us to assess what the particular effect is of each instrument.	92	9
201406	1711	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	And, fourth, ending reinvestments later also strikes me as a better risk-management strategy.	92	9
201406	1712	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Let’s compare two scenarios:  reinvestments end before liftoff versus the end of reinvestments is delayed until after liftoff.	92	9
201406	1713	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, assume that, in these two scenarios, the economy subsequently disappoints.	92	9
201406	1714	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	In the first case, when we end reinvestments first, we might have to reverse course.	92	9
201406	1715	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	In the second case, ending reinvestments later, disappointment about the outlook would cause expectations about the end of reinvestments to be pushed out.	92	9
201406	1716	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	That would keep the balance sheet larger for longer, and that would act as an automatic stabilizer in terms of supporting economic activity, which I think would be desirable.	92	9
201406	1717	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	In terms of how to specify the end of reinvestments, my original thinking was maybe to specify a level of interest rates as a threshold or a trigger, but after talking to the Vice Chairman—not myself, but Stan—I concluded that retaining some flexibility was a better approach.	92	9
201406	1718	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	So I would favor general language to the effect that reinvestment is expected to continue until short-term interest rates are raised significantly above zero and the FOMC is significantly closer to meeting its dual-mandate objectives.	92	9
201406	1719	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I’m not wedded to any particular language, but I think keeping it relatively vague so we have some flexibility makes more sense.	92	9
201406	1720	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	So, Stan, you did convince me.	92	9
201406	1721	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	In terms of ending reinvestments all at once or more gradually, I think that depends on timing and circumstances.	92	9
201406	1722	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	If you were to adjust reinvestment in 2015, you probably would end it outright because the amount of maturing agency MBS is pretty modest, about $20 billion per month.	92	9
201406	1723	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	But if the end of reinvestment doesn’t occur until 2016, then you’re talking about a much bigger end, and so in that case you might want to taper it because you’re not really sure what such a large end might mean.	92	9
201406	1724	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I also think the particular circumstances of the economy at the time would be very important.	92	9
201406	1725	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	So I don’t think we have to really foreshadow exactly how we would do it at this point in time.	92	9
201406	1726	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	The second issue I want to focus on is the federal funds rate.	92	9
201406	1727	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Here I have a strong preference for revamping how we calculate the effective funds rate, adding the overnight Eurodollar borrowing as part of the calculation, and I want to substitute this new methodology for the current effective federal funds rate rather than having a new rate and an old rate.	92	9
201406	1728	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I favor moving to a single improved rate.	92	9
201406	1729	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	As Governor Powell has pointed out, moving to a single improved rate helps us considerably with the federal funds rate as a reference rate.	92	9
201406	1730	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	If we make the switch, then we have a rate that’s more robust that trillions of dollars of derivatives contracts reference.	92	9
201406	1731	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	If we keep the old rate and have a new rate, we still have this problem that we have all of these derivative contracts referencing this old, infirm rate.	92	9
201406	1732	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I think we found with LIBOR that there’s a tremendous amount of inertia.	92	9
201406	1733	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Everyone knows LIBOR is a troubled reference rate, yet people are still using LIBOR in all of their derivatives contracts.	92	9
201406	1734	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	So I would prefer to avoid the problem of forcing the transition to the new reference rate by just actually giving people an improved reference rate, and then it happens simultaneously and we’re done with that problem.	92	9
201406	1735	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I view the benefits of forcing the switch as large, relative to the risks of contract frustration.	92	9
201406	1736	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	My reading is that the contract frustration risks are very low because most contracts simply say the effective federal funds rate is what the Federal Reserve says the effective federal funds rate is.	92	9
201406	1737	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	And, second, in terms of the substance, the new rate will be very close.	92	9
201406	1738	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Over the past four years, it averages less than 1 basis point difference from the old federal funds rate.	92	9
201406	1739	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	So both in terms of the legal reading but also in terms of the difference in the two rates, it seems like just moving to the new rate makes the most sense.	92	9
201406	1740	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	With respect to the issue that changing to the new rate will make it hard down the road to move back to the old definition of the federal funds rate—I heard people express that as a concern once our balance sheet normalizes—I think this exaggerates the degree of difficulty of going back to the old federal funds rate sometime in the future.	92	9
201406	1741	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	If the federal funds rate market deepens again as our balance sheet normalizes, I think it wouldn’t be that hard to move back to the old definition and just explain that we’re now moving back to the old definition because the funds market is much deeper now.	92	9
201406	1742	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	It’s a much better reference rate.	92	9
201406	1743	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	It’s much less idiosyncratic.	92	9
201406	1744	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	And so we’re moving back for those reasons.	92	9
201406	1745	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I don’t think that constrains us very much.	92	9
201406	1746	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	The third issue I want to discuss is the issue of our target.	92	9
201406	1747	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	My own view is that we should be targeting the general level of money market rates rather than the federal funds rate.	92	9
201406	1748	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	The federal funds rate has gotten pretty idiosyncratic.	92	9
201406	1749	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I’m with Governor Fischer on this—why are we holding onto this thing as a vestige of times past when what we really care about in terms of setting monetary policy is setting the general level of money market rates to actually influence financial market conditions?	92	9
201406	1750	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	So I would prefer to emphasize the general level of money market rates—and we could keep the federal funds rate around, you know, we don’t have to throw it out, but I would emphasize general money market rates.	92	9
201406	1751	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I think I’d prefer that over actually emphasizing the IOER rate or the overnight RRP rate, because those are administered rates.	92	9
201406	1752	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	One thing I do want to avoid, though, is having the Desk try to pin the federal funds rate to a particular level and moving the overnight RRP and IOER rates around on a day-to-day basis.	92	9
201406	1753	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I don’t really see the benefit, in terms of affecting financial conditions, of small movements of these administered rates just to try to pin the federal funds rate to a particular rate.	92	9
201406	1754	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I think that what we really have to emphasize here is the control of financial market conditions, and so the simplest regime that generates good control of financial market conditions is what I’m for.	92	9
201406	1755	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	So that means a range for general money market rates, and as long as the rates stay within that range, then I wouldn’t see that you’d need to adjust the administered rates except when you’re trying to implement a policy change.	92	9
201406	1756	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	The fourth issue is with respect to caps on the overnight RRP facility.	92	9
201406	1757	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I think the staff made it very clear there are lots of ways to do it.	92	9
201406	1758	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	My emphasis would be on having caps that do not bind in peacetime, or noncrisis periods, but bind in wartime—crisis periods when we want to limit the inflow into the overnight RRP facility, to limit the upward spikes in riskier money market rates.	92	9
201406	1759	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I want a regime that’s well designed for the most common case, peacetime, rather than overengineered in a way that creates unnecessary frictions in peacetime just to be slightly better in wartime situations that might never occur.	92	9
201406	1760	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I think we’re overemphasizing, a little bit, the risk of this future financial crisis, and I don’t want to design a very complex mechanism that only is relevant on one day out of 1,000 days.	92	9
201406	1761	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	It just seems sort of backward.	92	9
201406	1762	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	In my mind, an ideal regime would have no caps in peacetime, except for a high overall limit that you would never expect to reach, and then in wartime a system of caps that was automatically triggered by market conditions when stress conditions developed.	92	9
201406	1763	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	In other words, what I’d prefer to have is an arrangement in which the caps automatically get triggered by a spread in interest rates.	92	9
201406	1764	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	So if the spread between risky rates and risk-free rates widens, the caps automatically come into place.	92	9
201406	1765	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, I know the staff hasn’t proposed this.	92	9
201406	1766	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	It’s probably too complicated to be easily realized.	92	9
201406	1767	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	You’d always have the risk that you might not be sure that the caps would be forthcoming in all circumstances.	92	9
201406	1768	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I would encourage the staff to consider whether a regime like this was feasible, but I’m going to confine my remaining comments to the construct as outlined in the staff memo.	92	9
201406	1769	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I would generally be pretty indifferent between individual caps and aggregate caps.	92	9
201406	1770	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	It seems like the staff nailed the distinction.	92	9
201406	1771	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Individual caps have the benefit of certainty for the investor.	92	9
201406	1772	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	The aggregate caps have the value that you get the pooling advantage, and so they’re more efficient in that sense.	92	9
201406	1773	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I get the sense from reading the staff’s report that they lean in the direction of aggregate caps.	92	9
201406	1774	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I certainly get a sense around the table that we as a collective group lean in favor of aggregate caps.	92	9
201406	1775	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	So I’m perfectly happy to go with the sense of the Committee and go with an aggregate cap.	92	9
201406	1776	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Finally, I have just a few thoughts on the whole issue of the overnight RRP facility, which has gotten a lot of comments today.	92	9
201406	1777	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I think the consensus around the table, as I hear it, is that we want to use the overnight RRP facility to establish a floor on rates to enhance our credibility in terms of monetary policy control, but we want to keep it pretty small in terms of its footprint in the market.	92	9
201406	1778	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	And so that implies that we’re going to have to keep the spread relatively wide to limit take-up.	92	9
201406	1779	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	My view is that a spread of 20 or even 30 basis points would probably be effective in terms of setting a floor and maintaining monetary policy control.	92	9
201406	1780	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I think if we did that we could be pretty comfortable that we weren’t going to get a facility that was large in some sense.	92	9
201406	1781	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I don’t view, in the context of the US financial system, a facility that is $200 billion or $300 billion as large.	92	9
201406	1782	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I don’t know what the total amount of financial assets outstanding in the United States is, but it’s probably $60 trillion.	92	9
201406	1783	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	So if you had a facility that was $200 billion, I think that would be not large but pretty trivial in the context of the US economy.	92	9
201406	1784	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Also, I think we should make no commitment to making it permanent, but I would prefer not to make a commitment to making it temporary, either.	92	9
201406	1785	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I would just keep it open.	92	9
201406	1786	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I think we’re going to learn by having this facility in place, and maybe it will work better, in more miraculous ways, than we anticipate, or maybe it will work worse, and I don’t think anything we say today is really going to bind future Committees.	92	9
201406	1787	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	And so I think I’d keep it open and not lean one way or the other in terms of what’s going to happen over the longer term.	92	9
201406	1788	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1789	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201406	1790	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	President George.	92	9
201406	1791	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1792	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	Like others, I found the discussion from April and again today to be very helpful, and I remain open to considering this mix of tools as we go through normalization.	92	9
201406	1793	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	I am very comfortable with how the Chair has described a centrist approach in thinking about this.	92	9
201406	1794	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	I do think, though, that we’ll need to be clearer about our intentions regarding the ultimate size of the balance sheet.	92	9
201406	1795	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	When I look at the draft that the staff included of possible revised policy normalization principles, the phrase that indicates we will hold no more securities than necessary to implement monetary policy efficiently and effectively is in brackets, which suggests it’s an issue that we’re going to need to discuss.	92	9
201406	1796	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	My own view remains generally consistent with the 2011 principles that we affirmed just last year, which say that we intend to eventually hold no more securities than needed and reduce reserves to the smallest levels consistent with the efficient implementation of policy.	92	9
201406	1797	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	One aspect of the normalization discussion and this use of overnight RRPs that makes me uncomfortable, as others have noted, is the substantially larger footprint we could have outside of the banking system, and I would align myself with Governor Tarullo’s views and counsel in this regard.	92	9
201406	1798	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	Transacting directly with nonbank counterparties raises concerns about where we would draw the line, and while money market funds seem a natural boundary today, I could see over time that this pressure around fairness could grow and cause us to consider insurance companies, nonfinancial corporations, and pension funds as direct counterparties.	92	9
201406	1799	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	So, although as a practical matter the footprint may need to expand in the near term, I think steps to reduce the size of our balance sheet should remain a central tenet of our normalization strategy.	92	9
201406	1800	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	To address the specific questions, in terms of the federal funds rate, returning the balance sheet to its pre-crisis levels relative to GDP with a small amount of excess reserves calls, I think, for maintaining a role for the federal funds rate throughout the normalization process.	92	9
201406	1801	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	At the same time, control of overnight rates will require, at least for a time, the use of an ON RRP facility.	92	9
201406	1802	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	In terms of communications, I think continued reference to the federal funds rate is appropriate even though it may not serve as the primary tool during the early stages following liftoff.	92	9
201406	1803	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	As a practical matter, the ON RRP rate will need to serve that purpose given the size of our balance sheet and the use of IOER, but I would prefer to take an approach that maintains a wide spread in relation to the IOER rate.	92	9
201406	1804	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	I also support the development of an expanded federal funds rate, though I would prefer that we move cautiously before adopting it as any kind of formal target of policy.	92	9
201406	1805	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	Regarding circuit breakers, I am comfortable with aggregate caps, with a market-based pricing mechanism designed to become activated when the cap is reached.	92	9
201406	1806	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	However, again, I think a smaller balance sheet will naturally take us in this direction, and so, for that reason, I think we should remain focused on steps to reduce that balance sheet.	92	9
201406	1807	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	And, finally, regarding reinvestment policy, it seems to me that the economy has not disappointed relative to our expectations last June when we reaffirmed the plan to cease reinvestments prior to liftoff.	92	9
201406	1808	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	If you remember, last June, the midpoint of our SEPs projected headline PCE inflation to be 1 percent in 2013 and the unemployment rate to be 7¼ percent.	92	9
201406	1809	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	Of course, unemployment fell more quickly, and inflation was above these projections, and given subsequent improvement in the unemployment rate and increased inflation, I don’t see a compelling reason to deviate from the plan of ceasing reinvestments prior to liftoff.	92	9
201406	1810	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	However, given that the primary dealer survey shows market expectations have shifted, we might consider redirecting maturing Treasury and MBS securities into shorter-dated Treasury securities.	92	9
201406	1811	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	That would allow us to maintain an elevated level of the balance sheet, but also provide for a more rapid runoff after liftoff.	92	9
201406	1812	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Could I just ask a question?	92	9
201406	1813	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Did you say that last June we had reiterated something about ceasing reinvestments?	92	9
201406	1814	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	We affirmed the broad principles around our 2011—	92	9
201406	1815	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	But not the specifics around that.	92	9
201406	1816	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	We said—	92	9
201406	1817	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	That’s right.	92	9
201406	1818	2014-06-18	meeting	POTTER	The tactics—in the press conference, it was clear that they were sort of suspended.	92	9
201406	1819	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	And without distinguishing which were principles and which were tactics, the sequencing I saw as being the broad outlines of the principles that we had laid out in that exit strategy of 2011.	92	9
201406	1820	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	The Chairman, though, explicitly said something about agency MBS being—	92	9
201406	1821	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	I believe the Chairman said we would not sell MBS, and I think he said eventually we would have a smaller balance sheet, but that other aspects of it were up for reconsideration.	92	9
201406	1822	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Right.	92	9

201406	1825	2014-06-18	meeting	GEORGE	But he didn’t take off the table that we would stop reinvestments.	92	9

201406	1838	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	President Mester.	92	9
201406	1839	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1840	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	I appreciate the opportunity of joining this august group.	92	9
201406	1841	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Of course, as the Chair noted, I have attended quite a few of these meetings during my career, but up to now that was as a policy adviser, not as a policymaker.	92	9
201406	1842	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	As if there were any doubt, preparing for this meeting underscored the fact that while the physical distance from my former chair behind President Plosser to my current seat beside him is only a couple of feet, the real distance is far greater.	92	9
201406	1843	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	So I’m looking forward to contributing what I can to the discussions and formulation of monetary policy, to learning from all of you, and to working with you in my new role.	92	9
201406	1844	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	To that end, I want to add my thanks to the staff for the very helpful memos this time and last time on normalization.	92	9
201406	1845	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	It was a heroic task to find the common ground in the discussion at the previous meeting, but you did it.	92	9
201406	1846	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	And I found the memos helped both me and my staff focus on the open issues.	92	9
201406	1847	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Now, in thinking through the issues, it became clear to me that the communications surrounding the choices we make about normalization are going to be nearly as important, if not equally important, as the economics behind the choices.	92	9
201406	1848	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	In many cases, there is going to be a tradeoff.	92	9
201406	1849	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	The more complex methods of conducting policy might afford tighter control of interest rates, but they are going to be considerably more difficult to explain to the public, which in my view mitigates the benefits of more complicated methods.	92	9
201406	1850	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	It also seems clear that there is going to have to be learning by doing.	92	9
201406	1851	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Although we have been testing our tools, which is prudent, the testing is, by necessity, small and in an environment in which we haven’t been raising interest rates.	92	9
201406	1852	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	There are going to be surprises along the way.	92	9
201406	1853	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	I am confident we will be able to raise interest rates with our tools, but precisely how much control of interest rates our tools provide, or how much we want to achieve as we begin raising rates, is unknowable until we are doing it.	92	9
201406	1854	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	So I think we need to be guided by experience as we implement the transition back to more-normal policymaking.	92	9
201406	1855	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	These considerations make me think it’s better to start with simpler methods, and then, as we gain more experience and we find those methods aren’t working quite the way we’d like, we can add complexity.	92	9
201406	1856	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	As a contingency, I think we need to be prepared to use the full range of our tools, including term deposits and asset sales as needed.	92	9
201406	1857	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Turning to the questions, on question 1, my preference is that we communicate the stance of policy in terms of a range for the federal funds rate, or an expanded measure of it, rather than by administered rates.	92	9
201406	1858	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Communicating in terms of market rates rather than administered rates makes clear that it’s the effect of monetary policy on market interest rates and the transmission of those to the economy that’s important.	92	9
201406	1859	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	While we can trivially hit an IOER rate target, since we set the IOER rate, this doesn’t solve the problem of what IOER target will produce the effect on the economy that we are seeking.	92	9
201406	1860	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Another reason I favor communication based on a target funds rate range is that it will provide continuity as we transition from the period of normalization into a longer-run framework in which policy is formulated in terms of a fed funds rate target or similar market rate.	92	9
201406	1861	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Such a framework is my preference at this point.	92	9
201406	1862	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	That said, I realize there are measurement challenges with the federal funds rate as currently formulated.	92	9
201406	1863	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	With little trading in the market, the rate can be idiosyncratic and could be decoupled from other market rates.	92	9
201406	1864	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	So I’m open to thinking about an expanded version that would take into account a broader set of trades like Eurodollar transactions.	92	9
201406	1865	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	But if we go in that direction, I think it’s going to be important for us to explain carefully why we are doing it, and to explain this earlier rather than later, along the suggested time frame in the memo.	92	9
201406	1866	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	We certainly need to do it before liftoff to avoid the appearance that we are redefining the target just because we failed to hit it, which would undermine our credibility.	92	9
201406	1867	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	I prefer setting a range for the funds rate target at this point and communicating that we will be using IOER and ON RRP as the tools to support achieving that target range.	92	9
201406	1868	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	We can add term deposits or asset sales if we find we need more control over market rates.	92	9
201406	1869	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	I note that we are currently formulating policy using a target range rather than a point target.	92	9
201406	1870	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	The public has accepted it.	92	9
201406	1871	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	And the economic benefit of hitting a point target would seem to be swamped by the potential credibility issues posed if we consistently missed the point target, and by the complexity or size of operations that might be needed to hit the point target.	92	9
201406	1872	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	So I don’t see any advantage at this point of moving back from a range to a point target, especially at the early stage of normalization.	92	9
201406	1873	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	We can always narrow the range as normalization proceeds and the balance sheet is reduced to a size that gives us more control over the rate.	92	9
201406	1874	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	On question 2, regarding the overnight RRP program, I do have some concerns about the full-allotment facility.	92	9
201406	1875	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Even aside from the financial-stability concerns during times of financial stress, during normal times a full-allotment facility would decrease the potential for a revival of the funds market over the longer run.	92	9
201406	1876	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	And I think it will be very difficult to turn back once we go to a large-scale facility.	92	9
201406	1877	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	In addition, such a facility implies a sizable expansion of implementation of policy through nonbank counterparties, including money market mutual funds, whose accounting rules we have criticized.	92	9
201406	1878	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	So my preference would be to limit the size of the program and avoid committing at this point to a permanent ON RRP facility.	92	9
201406	1879	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	I would also favor imposing aggregate caps that would be binding more often than not, even in normal times, but particularly as we start the normalization process.	92	9
201406	1880	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Such a binding limit on the size during normal times could have an additional benefit during times of financial stress—namely, having seen binding size limits during normal times, market participants may view any circuit breakers we choose to impose to limit inflows during times of financial stress as being more credible.	92	9
201406	1881	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	And then they might make contingency plans for binding caps and rely less on the RRPs.	92	9
201406	1882	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	On question 3, given the estimated effects, it probably doesn’t make that much difference economically whether reinvestments are simply stopped or gradually reduced once a decision is announced.	92	9
201406	1883	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Regarding timing relative to the first rate increase, the exit-strategy principles of June 2011 indicated the Committee would likely first stop buying assets, then stop reinvesting, and then begin raising interest rates.	92	9
201406	1884	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	And I guess there is a certain salience to that given that the size of the balance sheet is related to the degree of accommodation.	92	9
201406	1885	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	But that timing presents a communications challenge.	92	9
201406	1886	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	I think it would be hard to announce an end to reinvestments without bringing forward market expectations of liftoff.	92	9
201406	1887	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	The cessation of reinvestments would essentially be the first tightening move, if it came before liftoff.	92	9
201406	1888	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	And since my preference would be to use interest rates as our main policy tool, I would prefer to end reinvestments either at the time of the first increase in short-term interest rates or, if the other participants preferred, after the first rate increase.	92	9
201406	1889	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	On question 4, as I indicated earlier, I’m open to thinking about an expanded version of the funds rate.	92	9
201406	1890	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	But if we do redefine it, it’s going to be important to explain why we are doing it and to do it well before liftoff.	92	9
201406	1891	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Coming into the meeting, I didn’t have strong feelings about whether to rename the expanded rate the funds rate or to publish two rates, but I found Governor Powell’s and Vice Chairman Dudley’s discussion persuasive that it may be better just to publish one rate.	92	9
201406	1892	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	I would prefer that we base the expanded rate on the FR-2420 data when those data become available to avoid the perception that we are targeting borrowing costs associated with foreign entities or money market mutual funds.	92	9
201406	1893	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Let me end with a final thought.	92	9
201406	1894	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Clear communications are an essential ingredient in a smooth transition process.	92	9
201406	1895	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Our communications need to be as clear as possible about what methods we plan to use and why.	92	9
201406	1896	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	They also need to convey the idea that, as we gain experience through the normalization process, we are going to make adjustments to the mix of our tools as needed in order to achieve our mandated goals.	92	9
201406	1897	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	As I said, the communications issues are not trivial.	92	9
201406	1898	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	To help, I think we might consider asking the staff to issue a working paper that lays out some of the normalization considerations.	92	9
201406	1899	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	This could be similar to the working-paper primer the Board staff issued early last year about projections for the Federal Reserve’s balance sheet and income.	92	9
201406	1900	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	As a Reserve Bank staffer, I found it helpful to refer people to this paper when they had questions.	92	9
201406	1901	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Of course, such a working paper would not replace any official communications by the Committee and the Chair, but it might be a useful way to convey the idea that we are aware there are different approaches and several considerations when selecting an approach to normalization, and that adjustments could very well be necessary as we proceed.	92	9
201406	1902	2014-06-18	meeting	MESTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1903	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201406	1904	2014-06-18	meeting	YELLEN	President Lacker.	92	9
201406	1905	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201406	1906	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	First, a couple of general remarks.	92	9
201406	1907	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	After listening carefully to the rich discussion at our previous meeting and digesting a rich array of memos for this meeting, I remain unconvinced that we are going to need an overnight RRP program to ensure market rates rise when we raise the interest rate on excess reserves and the funds rate target.	92	9
201406	1908	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	We rely on some obvious arbitrage relationships for the vast majority of the links in the chain of economic relationships that make up the monetary policy transmission mechanism.	92	9
201406	1909	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	And I don’t see any reason why arbitrage isn’t going to work to keep the RP rate aligned with interbank rates like the IOER rate and the fed funds rate, and the staff hasn’t really explained a theory about why that wouldn’t happen, at least to my knowledge.	92	9
201406	1910	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Moreover, I think routine use at a scale like what we’ve seen runs the risk of inducing significant restructuring of money markets, a concern many have alluded to here.	92	9
201406	1911	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	I think flows into the ON RRP facility are going to be potentially unpredictable both in normal times and in times of stress, as Governor Tarullo has emphasized.	92	9
201406	1912	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	I don’t think we are close to understanding them.	92	9
201406	1913	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	I’d point to one question that remains open.	92	9
201406	1914	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	The staff, particularly in New York, documented shifts in funding in the sense of cash lending that seemed to be a response to our program.	92	9
201406	1915	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	What is happening on the collateral financing side remains a mystery, and there doesn’t seem to have been much staff work into where the collateral that might otherwise have been financed by the money market funds that are lending to us now is being financed or held.	92	9
201406	1916	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Accordingly, I would prefer to use an overnight RRP facility only as a temporary contingency program.	92	9
201406	1917	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	In my view, we should start raising rates the usual way.	92	9
201406	1918	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	We should raise the interest rate on excess reserves by 15 or 25 basis points—so, take it to 40 or 50 basis points.	92	9
201406	1919	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	We should raise the upper end of the range of the target federal funds rate accordingly to either 40 or 50 basis points.	92	9
201406	1920	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	We should leave the overnight RRP rate at 5 or maybe 10 basis points— maybe increase it 5 basis points.	92	9
201406	1921	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	And when we did that, we would say that we may increase the ON RRP rate at future meetings.	92	9
201406	1922	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	We’d leave ourselves open with that option.	92	9
201406	1923	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	We would just leave that on the table.	92	9
201406	1924	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Now, we will learn in short order whether the obvious arbitrage relationship is effective or not.	92	9
201406	1925	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	If it is, we can keep the overnight RRP rate at a deep backstop of 50, maybe 75 basis points below the IOER rate.	92	9
201406	1926	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	And the concerns everyone has about an excessively large program will be answered.	92	9
201406	1927	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	It will be a relatively small backstop, just in case it’s necessary.	92	9
201406	1928	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	So what if that doesn’t happen?	92	9
201406	1929	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	What if the RP rate doesn’t rise—that’s the possibility to think about.	92	9
201406	1930	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Well, at the next meeting, we raise the overnight RRP rate to 20 basis points below the IOER rate.	92	9
201406	1931	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	For our macroeconomic objectives, our mandate objectives, the delay is going to be inconsequential.	92	9
201406	1932	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	I don’t think one meeting, in terms of the liftoff date, is going to matter much one way or another.	92	9
201406	1933	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	The big risk is what I’d call the egg-on-the-face risk.	92	9
201406	1934	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	I don’t think Bill English used this term, but this is the idea that we announce we are tightening conditions, and some market conditions don’t tighten.	92	9
201406	1935	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Well, I don’t think D-Day is the right way to approach this first increase.	92	9
201406	1936	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	If we held it in suspense, made it a big surprise, and then attacked financial markets with overwhelming force—I don’t think that’s the way to do it.	92	9
201406	1937	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	[Laughter]	92	9
201406	1938	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Instead, we could do something a little more modest.	92	9
201406	1939	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	We could just say we are making an adjustment in preparation for a plan to raise interest rates and adjust financial conditions.	92	9
201406	1940	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	We could do it without saying, “This is the big day, everybody.”	92	9
201406	1941	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	When I was a kid, we’d get the TV and we’d watch John Glenn lift off and everything—T would get to zero, and the rocket would light up, but it would just stay there for 5 or 10 seconds before it started moving up.	92	9
201406	1942	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	[Laughter].	92	9
201406	1943	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	I think we’ll get the rocket up.	92	9
201406	1944	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	If we do this, I think we’ll learn pretty quickly whether we need a big-scale program, a medium-scale program, or what.	92	9
201406	1945	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	And given everyone’s discomfort around here with a big program, I think we’d want to do the learning sooner rather than later.	92	9
201406	1946	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Let’s get our learning done right at the beginning, and it’s just going to take one move and we’ll figure it out.	92	9
201406	1947	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	So that’s just a general comment.	92	9
201406	1948	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Let me grind my way through the questions here.	92	9
201406	1949	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	On the question about how we communicate, given the configuration toward which I think we are going to head—IOER and a target federal funds rate that is anchored at the top by the IOER rate of, say, 25 basis points— there is an equivalence between describing things in terms of IOER and describing things in terms of the funds rate.	92	9
201406	1950	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	We can even describe it in terms of the discount rate, for that matter.	92	9
201406	1951	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	But I think the logical thing, given the governance reality that the Committee controls the funds rate target, is that we continue to describe policy in terms of the funds rate or some suitably defined interest rate and let the IOER rate be set by the Board in a related action.	92	9
201406	1952	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	That formulation has worked very well for the discount rate, and I think we should continue doing that.	92	9
201406	1953	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	On the question about a point versus a range, unless the range gets much smaller, I think we should stick with a range.	92	9
201406	1954	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Later on, when reserves get smaller, we can shift to a point.	92	9
201406	1955	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	I’d be against stating a target in terms of general money market rates.	92	9
201406	1956	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	And I’d just remind you of a bit of history: We started targeting the funds rate because of controversy surrounding the accountability of the System Open Market Account manager and disputes about whether they were faithfully executing the charge we had given them.	92	9
201406	1957	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I trust the System Open Market Account manager.	92	9
201406	1958	2014-06-18	meeting		[Laughter]	92	9
201406	1959	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	With all due respect—There’s an important element of what are we asking them to do, how do we know they’re doing what we have asked them to do, and so on, so I think it is important to keep a specific range that we can monitor.	92	9
201406	1960	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	On the question about circuit breakers, I don’t think circuit breakers on a fixed rate, full- allotment overnight RRP program are capable of addressing the financial-stability issues that some have raised in this context.	92	9
201406	1961	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	If investors want to flee a particular counterparty, or a particular class of counterparties, depriving them of the option of Federal Reserve Bank overnight RRP investments is hardly going to stop them.	92	9
201406	1962	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	They have short-term Treasury securities.	92	9
201406	1963	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	They have money market funds.	92	9
201406	1964	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	They’ve got bank deposits.	92	9
201406	1965	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	And that is just in the United States.	92	9
201406	1966	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Indeed, most of the bank runs in 2008 were from one bank to another or from one counterparty to another in the same asset class.	92	9
201406	1967	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	So I just don’t think this is worth troubling ourselves about.	92	9
201406	1968	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Now, on the other hand, I do think we should limit the size of the program, if we’re going down that road, and so I think we should impose an explicit quantitative limit on the size of the program, if only because of the finite size of our balance sheet.	92	9
201406	1969	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	I mean, if we go to full allotment, it would raise questions, what do we do if we get everybody showing up, and  running an auction like that described under option 2?	92	9
201406	1970	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	In our earlier discussion, we had a really interesting exchange about interest rates.	92	9
201406	1971	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Stopping out at the cap and then having an auction that drives interest rates down—this would be a mechanism to reduce the rate of return on ON RRPs in order to discourage people from shifting into them.	92	9
201406	1972	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	The obvious question is, why don’t we just reduce interest rates if we don’t want investors fleeing the assets they’re in?	92	9
201406	1973	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	That’s what we usually do in a crisis anyway.	92	9
201406	1974	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	So I’m not sure that’s germane here.	92	9
201406	1975	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	On the question about reinvestment, I’m in President George’s camp of viewing elements of the exit strategy that we articulated in 2011 that have not been specifically refuted as standing as implicit commitments of ours.	92	9
201406	1976	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	We indicated that we’d begin normalization by ending reinvestments and only later raising interest rates.	92	9
201406	1977	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	I think the macroeconomic implications of whether we start running off our portfolio several months before or several months after we start raising rates are likely to be negligible.	92	9
201406	1978	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	And I think that the staff’s analysis supported the idea that this is not terribly consequential.	92	9
201406	1979	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	But I do think it would erode our credibility to fail to follow through on the guidance we provided several years ago.	92	9
201406	1980	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Forward guidance is really central to how we conduct policy these days.	92	9
201406	1981	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	I would think that at the margin we would always be reluctant to renege on past statements.	92	9
201406	1982	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	I think, as a general principle, there ought to be something at stake.	92	9
201406	1983	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	And to me, the macroeconomic difference doesn’t seem to be worth it.	92	9
201406	1984	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	It just seems like there is little to gain there.	92	9
201406	1985	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	On the question about an expanded federal funds rate, I came in having been left with the impression by some staff memo—I can’t remember which one—that there were enough legal differences between federal funds and Eurodollars to make it important to establish a new rate, but Governor Powell and Vice Chairman Dudley seemed persuasive about those issues, so I could easily be persuaded that we go with a single new rate.	92	9
201406	1986	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	I have two final thoughts.	92	9
201406	1987	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	The staff has spent an enormous amount of time and effort on these memos, and I greatly appreciate all the time and energy they have devoted to this.	92	9
201406	1988	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	We have spent a great deal of time on this as well.	92	9
201406	1989	2014-06-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Not as much as they have.	92	9
201406	1990	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	First, there’s a sense in which the memos have been focused on a narrow perspective.	92	9
201406	1991	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	The issues we’re talking about—should the central bank offer moneylike liabilities to counterparties outside the banking industry—this goes back a couple of centuries to the debates about the banking school and the currency school, 100 percent reserves, narrow banking, and the like, and there is a broader debate here and a broader set of economic issues about how central banks should be structured that we haven’t really touched on.	92	9
201406	1992	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Second—and this is my last thought—I’m sure there are market participants who are dying to know about the operational mechanics of our exit.	92	9
201406	1993	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	But the closer I get to September, the more I think that the operational mechanics are not what most Americans want to know about our exit strategy.	92	9
201406	1994	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	I think they are interested in when it’s going to happen.	92	9
201406	1995	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	I think they will believe us when we say it depends.	92	9
201406	1996	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	But I think they are going to want to know what it depends on—is it the level of resource utilization?	92	9
201406	1997	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Is it the rate of change of resource utilization, or consumption, or output, or the like?	92	9
201406	1998	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	How does inflation figure in?	92	9
201406	1999	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	Does inflation have to get high first, or are we going to nip incipient pressures in the bud?	92	9
201406	2000	2014-06-18	meeting	LACKER	I worry that the time we are spending on the mechanics of our exit are detracting from useful work that we could and perhaps should be devoting to the macroeconomics of our exit.	92	9
